Refutation of the Karramiyya on Power and Death
Nasafi refutes the Karramiyya claim about power and death.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand why the Karramiyya's distinction between power and other attributes with respect to death is logically unsustainable.

Core Idea
If power were part of life, death—not incapacity—would be its opposite.

The Karramiyya sect claimed that all attributes except power can remain with a dead person. Nasafi challenges this by showing that their justification—that power is part of life—leads to absurd consequences. This passage demonstrates how logical consistency refutes arbitrary theological distinctions.

Guided Path
1
Read the source passage
Read the Arabic first, then the translation. Notice the structure: statement of the Karramiyya position, their defense, and two refutation arguments.
2
Identify the two refutation moves
The first move is a counter-example: one could claim the opposite equally. The second is a logical proof: if power is part of life, its opposite is death, not incapacity, but incapacity coexists with life, so contradiction arises.
Focus on the second move as the stronger argument.
3
Reflect on the lesson
Consider why this argument is effective against the Karramiyya position. How does it show the importance of defining attributes and their opposites correctly?
This connects to broader kalam methodology.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وبطلان قول الكرامية حيث يجوزون ذلك كله إلا القدرة فإنها لا تجامع الموت عندهم، فأما ما وراء القدرة فيجوز اجتماعها مع الموت عندهم، وإذا طولبوا بالفرق زعموا أن القدرة هي من جملة الحياة، فأما العلم وما وراء ذلك من الصفات فليست من جملتها قيل لهم : وبم تنفصلون ممن عكس عليكم فادعي أن العلم والسمع والبصر من جملة الحياة، والقدرة ليست كذلك ؟ ثم نقول لهم : لو كان الأمر على ما تزعمون لكانت القدرة لا تفارق الحياة ولا يجامعها العجز الذي هو ضد القدرة، وحيث كان الأمر بخلافه دل على بطلان هذه المقالة. يحققه : أن القدرة لو كانت من جملة الحياة، لكان ضدها الموت لا العجز، ولو جاز اجتماع العجز والحياة لجاز اجتماع الموت والحياة لأن العجز كما يضاد القدرة يضاد الحياة التي من جملتها القدرة، وحيث لم يكن كذلك دل أن هذا القول باطل
And the invalidity of the statement of the Karramiyya when they permit all that except power (al-qudra), for it does not coexist with death according to them. As for what is beyond power, its coexistence with death is permissible according to them. And when they are demanded to differentiate, they claim that power is part of life (al-hayat), but knowledge and the attributes beyond that are not part of it. It is said to them: How do you distinguish from one who reverses upon you and claims that knowledge, hearing, and sight are part of life, and power is not? Then we say to them: If the matter were as you claim, power would not separate from life and incapacity (al-'ajz), which is the opposite of power, would not coexist with it. But since the matter is contrary, this indicates the invalidity of this claim. He verifies it: If power were part of life, its opposite would be death, not incapacity. And if the coexistence of incapacity and life were permissible, the coexistence of death and life would be permissible, because incapacity opposes both power and the life of which power is a part. And since it is not so, this indicates that this statement is false.
Source pages p. 359

Commentary
This passage refutes the Karramiyya sect's position that all attributes except power (qudra) can coexist with death. The author first states the Karramiyya claim: they allow all other attributes—like knowledge, hearing, sight—to remain with death, but power alone cannot. When pressed for a distinction, they argue that power is part of life (hayat) while other attributes are not. The refutation proceeds in two steps. First, a counter-argument is posed: one could just as well claim the opposite—that knowledge, hearing, and sight are part of life and power is not, showing the arbitrariness of their distinction. Second, the author proves the logical consequence: if power were truly part of life, then its direct opposite would be death, not incapacity ('ajz). But we observe that incapacity and life can coexist (e.g., a living being can be incapable), whereas death and life cannot coexist. Thus, since incapacity opposes both power and life, the Karramiyya position leads to contradiction and is invalid.

Key Terms
القدرة (al-qudra)
الحياة (al-hayat)
الموت (al-mawt)
العجز (al-'ajz)
الكرامية (al-Karramiyya)

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Power cannot coexist with death because it is part of life, while other attributes are not.
Correction: If power were part of life, its opposite would be death, not incapacity. Since incapacity (which opposes power) can coexist with life, the claim that power is part of life leads to contradiction.

Checkpoint
According to the refutation, if power were part of life, what would its opposite be?
A) Incapacity
B) Death
C) Knowledge
D) Ignorance

Key Takeaway
The Karramiyya position on power and death is invalid because it leads to the contradictory result that life and death can coexist.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
In what area of your life do you unconsciously limit God's power, thinking that it cannot coexist with certain circumstances? What is one specific step you can take today to remove that mental barrier?
?
This passage shows that logical inconsistency can invalidate a belief about God. Examine your own creed: Are there any beliefs you hold about Allah that, if followed to their logical conclusion, would lead to a contradiction? What would it cost you to correct that belief?

Refuting al-Salihi's Objection on Attributes Without Life
Nasafi refutes al-Salihi's claim that God cannot create attributes without first creating life.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand Nasafi's refutation of al-Salihi's claim that God would need life as a tool to create attributes, and why this argument misunderstands the limits of divine power.

Core Idea
God's power is not limited by rational impossibilities; attributes require a living subject by nature.

This lesson examines a subtle objection raised by al-Salihi, who argued that if attributes like power and knowledge can only exist in living beings, then God would need to create life first, making life a tool. Nasafi refutes this by pointing out that God is not described as having power to create impossible combinations, such as a substance without an accident. Understanding this clarifies the relationship between divine power and the nature of created things.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage and translation
Begin by reading the Arabic passage and its literal translation. Pay attention to al-Salihi's argument and Nasafi's response.
Note the three examples Nasafi gives in his refutation.
2
Identify the refutation's structure
Notice that Nasafi first summarizes al-Salihi's claim, then declares it corrupt, and then lists three things God cannot create as an analogy.
These examples show that the need for a substrate is not a limitation.
3
Connect to the larger principle
Reflect on how this refutation defends the principle that divine power extends only to what is rationally possible. Attributes requiring life is a rational necessity, not a weakness.
This distinguishes between incapacity and impossibility.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وكذا ما يقوله الصالحي: أن القدرة والعلم لو لم يصح وجودهما في غير الحي لكان الله تعالى، إذا أراد خلق القدرة أو العلم في شيء لما قدر عليه، ما لم يخلق فيه الحياة فيصير عاجزا عنه ويحتاج إلى خلق الحياة ،أولا، فيصير ذلك كالآلة له. وهذا كلام فاسد، فإن الله تعالى لا يوصف بالقدرة على خلق الجوهر متعريا عن العرض ولا على خلق العرض إلا في الجوهر، ولا على خلق مماسة في الجسم
And similarly what al-Salihi says: that if power and knowledge cannot exist in other than the living, then God Almighty, when He wants to create power or knowledge in a thing, would not be able to do so unless He first creates life in it. Then He becomes incapable of it and needs to create life first, and that becomes like a tool for Him. This is corrupt speech. For God Almighty is not described as having power to create a substance devoid of an accident, nor to create an accident except in a substance, nor to create contact (mumassa) in a body.
Source pages p. 360

Commentary
This passage refutes another argument from al-Salihi. He claimed that if power and knowledge can only exist in a living being (hayy), then God would be unable to create these attributes in something without first creating life in it, making life a necessary tool and thus limiting God's power. The refutation counters that this premise is wrong: God is not described as having power to create impossible things, such as a substance without any accident, or an accident without a substrate (jawhar), or contact (mumassa) in a body (since contact is a relation, not a created accident). The implied point is that power and knowledge are accidents that require a living subject; it is not a weakness that they cannot exist in a non-living thing—just as God cannot create a substance without any accident because that is a rational impossibility. Thus al-Salihi's objection is invalid because it misunderstands what is within divine power.

Key Terms
القدرة (al-qudra)
العلم (al-ilm)
الحياة (al-hayat)
الجوهر (al-jawhar)
العرض (al-'arad)
المماسة (al-mumassa)

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: God's inability to create an attribute without a living subject limits His power.
Correction: Nasafi clarifies that this inability is due to rational impossibility, not incapacity. God's power extends only to what is possible, and attributes requiring life is a natural necessity.

Checkpoint
How does Nasafi refute al-Salihi's claim that God would need life as a tool?
A) By affirming that life is a tool for God
B) By stating that God cannot create power and knowledge at all
C) By denying that attributes can only exist in living beings
D) By pointing out that God cannot create a substance without an accident

Key Takeaway
Nasafi refutes al-Salihi by showing that requiring life for attributes is a rational necessity, not a limitation of divine power.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Have you ever felt that God is ‘limited’ because He does not grant what you desire? In light of this lesson, do you think your desires might actually be rational impossibilities that even God does not will? How does accepting this humbly change your dua?
?
Nasafi says God cannot create a substance without an accident—this is not a flaw but the natural order. Are there areas in your life where you resist God's decreed order, expecting Him to act against His own consistent pattern? Will you submit to His wisdom, even when you cannot understand it?
?
The objection of al-Salihi sounds plausible at first. Where in your own thinking have you mistaken a rational necessity for a limitation? What would it cost you to admit that God's power is perfectly expressed in what He does, not in what you imagine He should do?

Refuting Self-Contradiction in Opposites
Objection and response about self-contradiction in opposites.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how a kalam argument can be refuted by showing it leads to a thing being opposite to itself.

Core Idea
A claim that forces a thing to be opposite to itself is self-defeating.

This passage presents a sophisticated objection-and-response typical of kalam reasoning. The author refutes an opponent's argument by showing that it leads to an absurd conclusion—namely, that a thing would be opposite to itself. By tracing the logical implication, the reader sees how the argument collapses.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage carefully
Read the Arabic passage once without pausing. Then read the translation. Notice the flow from the initial statement to the counter-argument.
The passage uses a conditional structure.
2
Identify the first absurd consequence
The author states that if something were opposite to its opposite, it would have to be opposite to itself. Find that line in the text.
This is the core claim.
3
Recognize the opponent's counter-argument
The opponent says: knowledge and death are opposites just as life and death are opposites. How does the author respond?
4
Follow the reductio ad absurdum
The author shows that if you accept that reasoning, then someone could claim life is not opposite to death because it doesn't oppose knowledge. See how the contradiction emerges.
This is the logical trap.
5
Summarize the refutation
Conclude that the opponent's claim leads to self-contradiction, so their initial argument is invalid.
This is a classic kalam technique.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ضده لكان ينبغي أن يكون الشيء مضادا لنفسه، لأنه ضد ضده الذي ضاده، والقول بكون الشيء مضادا لنفسه ظاهر الفساد. ويقال له: بم تنفصل عمن يقول : تقرر في أوائل العقول تضاد العلم والموت، حيث تقرر تضاد الحياة والموت؟ ولو جاز لك أن تقول هذا جاز لغيرك أن يقول : إن الحياة ليست بمضادة للموت إذ لو كانت مضادة للموت لضادت ما هو ضد الموت وهو العلم، وإذا لم تضاد ما هو ضد الموت لا تضاد الموت أيضا، وهذا فاسد فكذا الأول؟
Its opposite would necessitate that the thing be opposite to itself, because it is opposite to its opposite which opposed it, and the statement that a thing is opposite to itself is clearly corrupt. And it is said to him: How do you distinguish yourself from the one who says: It is established in the first principles of intellects the opposition of knowledge and death, just as the opposition of life and death is established? If you allow this statement, then someone else may say: Life is not opposite to death, because if it were opposite to death, it would oppose what is opposite to death, namely knowledge. And if it does not oppose what is opposite to death, it also does not oppose death. This is corrupt, so likewise the first?
Source pages p. 360

Commentary
This passage presents an objection-and-answer argument. The author begins by stating the absurd consequence of a certain claim: if something were opposite to its opposite, then it would have to be opposite to itself, which is clearly false. Then, an opponent is addressed: How do you differentiate yourself from someone who argues that knowledge and death are opposites just as life and death are opposites? The author explains that if you allow this reasoning, then someone else could argue that life is not opposite to death because if it were, it would have to oppose knowledge (which is opposite to death). Since life does not oppose knowledge, it cannot oppose death. This leads to a contradiction, so the initial argument is also corrupt. The passage thus refutes a specific line of reasoning by showing it leads to self-contradiction.

Key Terms
ضد
مضادة
تضاد
علم
موت
حياة

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some may think that if two pairs of things are both said to be opposites, they must be opposite in the same way and the relationship is transitive.
Correction: The passage shows that assuming transitivity leads to absurdity: life would have to oppose knowledge, which it does not, so the claim that knowledge and death are opposites is not valid in the same sense.

Checkpoint
According to the passage, what is the absurd consequence of claiming that something is opposite to its opposite?
A) The thing would be opposite to itself.
B) The thing would cease to exist.
C) The thing would become its own opposite.
D) The thing would have no opposite.

Key Takeaway
The argument demonstrates how to invalidate a claim by showing it forces a thing to be opposite to itself, a fundamental logical check in kalam.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Think of a time when you held a belief that, if followed to its logical end, would force you to contradict yourself. How does the method in this lesson expose the need to abandon that belief? Are you willing to apply this test to your own convictions, no matter how comfortable they are?
?
When you argue against someone's position, do you check whether your own reasoning leads to absurdity? The text shows the opponent's argument collapses because it contradicts itself. Will you commit to examining your own arguments with the same rigor before making claims about faith or theology?
?
The passage shows that logical consistency applies even to abstract concepts like knowledge and life. Are you willing to hold your own theological beliefs to the standard of logical consistency, even when it requires you to revise or reject ideas you have held for a long time? What specific belief will you examine today?

Objection on Necessary Knowledge of Opposites and Its Refutation
An objection about necessary knowledge of life-death opposition and the reply about interaction of opposites.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how the author refutes an objection about necessary knowledge of opposites by distinguishing between different oppositions and showing that coexistence with one thing does not guarantee coexistence with its opposite.

Core Idea
Not everything that coexists with one thing can coexist with its opposite.

This passage presents a theological objection and its refutation. The objector claims that life and death are known by necessity to be opposites. The author responds by pointing out that the objector's opponents also claim necessary knowledge that knowledge and death are opposites, so the objector must explain why his case is different. Then the author refutes a flawed inference, using the example of blackness and whiteness to show that coexistence with one does not imply coexistence with its opposite.

Guided Path
1
Read the objection carefully
Start by reading the objection: the claim that life and death are known by necessity to be opposites. Note the objector's appeal to 'necessary knowledge'.
This sets up the debate.
2
Understand the initial reply
Notice that the author first turns the tables: the objector's opponents also claim necessary knowledge that knowledge and death are opposites. The objector must distinguish his claim from theirs.
This shows a strategy of parity.
3
Examine the refutation of the inference
The objector infers that because knowledge and life can coexist, knowledge and death can also coexist. The author shows this inference is invalid with a counterexample: knowledge that a body is black can coexist with blackness but not with whiteness.
Focus on the logical form: not everything that coexists with one can coexist with its opposite.
4
Apply the principle
Reflect on the principle illustrated: coexistence with a thing does not guarantee coexistence with its opposite. Consider how this applies to the original objection about life and death.
This is the key takeaway.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ولو قال : أعلم بالضرورة أن الحياة والموت يتضادان. قيل: يعلم خصومك بالضرورة أن العلم والموت يتضادان ( كذا : القدرة والموت فانفصل عنهم، ويقال له: استدلالك بجواز اجتماع العلم والحياة وكذا القدرة والحياة على جواز مع الموت باطل، إذ ليس كل ما يجوز وجوده مع شيء يجوز وجوده مع ضده. فإن العلم بأن الجسم أسود ، والإخبار عن ذلك جائز الوجود في حال وجود السواد وليسا بجائز في الوجود في حال وجود البياض الذي هو ضد السواد.
And if he says: I know by necessity that life and death are opposites. It is said: Your opponents know by necessity that knowledge and death are opposites (and likewise: power and death—so distinguish yourself from them). And it is said to him: Your inference from the permissibility of the coexistence of knowledge and life, and likewise power and life, to the permissibility of coexistence with death is invalid, because not everything whose existence is permissible with something is permissible with its opposite. For the knowledge that a body is black, and the report about that, is permissible in the state of the existence of blackness, but they are not permissible in the state of the existence of whiteness which is the opposite of blackness.
Source pages p. 360

Commentary
This passage presents an objection and its refutation. The objector claims necessary knowledge that life and death are opposites. The author replies that the objector's opponents also claim necessary knowledge that knowledge and death are opposites, and similarly power and death—so the objector must distinguish his claim from theirs. Then, the author refutes a specific inference: the objector argues that because knowledge and life can coexist, knowledge and death can also coexist (since life and death are opposites). The author shows this inference is invalid by counterexample: the knowledge that a body is black can coexist with blackness, but cannot coexist with whiteness (the opposite of blackness). Thus, not everything that can coexist with one thing can coexist with its opposite. The passage demonstrates a key principle in reasoning about attributes and their opposites.

Key Terms
ضرورة
تضاد
علم
قدرة
حياة
موت
سواد
بياض

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: If A can coexist with B, then A can coexist with B's opposite.
Correction: The passage shows that knowledge that a body is black can coexist with blackness but not with whiteness (the opposite of blackness), disproving the general claim.

Checkpoint
What example does the author use to refute the claim that whatever can coexist with something can coexist with its opposite?
A) The knowledge that a body is black cannot coexist with whiteness.
B) The knowledge that a body is white cannot coexist with blackness.
C) Life cannot coexist with death.
D) Knowledge cannot coexist with ignorance.

Key Takeaway
The coexistence of something with one attribute does not imply its coexistence with that attribute's opposite.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Have you ever held a belief about God with such certainty that you dismissed opposing views as impossible, only to realize later that your reasoning was based on a false analogy? How does this lesson challenge you to examine the foundations of your certainty?
?
If you claim that God's mercy and justice cannot coexist because they seem opposite, how does this logical principle about coexistence with opposites force you to reconsider? What assumptions about God's attributes might you be projecting from human experience?
?
When you face a contradiction between what you think is necessary and what revelation teaches, will you humbly adjust your logic, or will you stubbornly insist on your own reasoning? This lesson shows a scholar willing to refine inference—are you?

Refutation of al-Salihi's Argument on Power, Knowledge, and Life
Al-Salihi's argument and its refutation via analogies.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how the author refutes al-Salihi's claim that requiring life for power and knowledge limits God's power.

Core Idea
God's power is not limited by the order of creation; life is a necessary condition, not a tool.

Al-Salihi argued that if power and knowledge can only exist in living beings, then God would need to create life first, making life a tool that limits His power. The author refutes this by drawing analogies to other necessary orders in creation, such as the requirement that accidents exist in substances, showing that such conditions are not limitations but part of how things are created.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage and translation
First, read the Arabic passage and its literal translation to understand the structure of the argument and refutation.
Notice the structure: al-Salihi's claim, then the author's response with multiple analogies.
2
Identify al-Salihi's argument
Identify the premise (power/knowledge only in living things) and the conclusion (God would need life as a tool, implying limitation).
The argument is based on a hypothetical conditional.
3
Study the refutation analogies
Examine the three analogies: substance without accident, accident only in substance, contact between bodies. Understand why these are impossible and how they parallel the life requirement.
Each analogy shows a necessary condition that is not a limitation on God.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وكذا ما يقوله الصالحي : أن القدرة والعلم لو لم يصح وجودهما في غير الحي لكان الله تعالى، إذا أراد خلق القدرة أو العلم في شيء لما قدر عليه، ما لم يخلق فيه الحياة فيصير عاجزا عنه ويحتاج إلى خلق الحياة ،أولا، فيصير ذلك كالآلة له. وهذا كلام فاسد، فإن الله تعالى لا يوصف بالقدرة على خلق الجوهر متعريا عن العرض ولا على خلق العرض إلا في الجوهر، ولا على خلق مماسة في الجسم بدون خلق مماسة أخرى في جسم آخر، لاستحالة اجتماع الشيء مع ما يفارقه ومفارقته لما يجامعه وهذا كله محال فكذا الأول.
And likewise what al-Salihi says: that if power and knowledge were not valid to exist in other than the living, then God, when He wills to create power or knowledge in something, would not be able to do so unless He creates life in it, so He would become incapable of it and would need to create life first, thus that would become like a tool for Him. This speech is corrupt, because God is not described as having power to create a substance devoid of an accident, nor to create an accident except in a substance, nor to create contact in a body without creating another contact in another body, due to the impossibility of a thing combining with what separates from it and separating from what combines with it—and all this is impossible, so likewise the first.
Source pages p. 360

Commentary
This passage presents an argument by al-Salihi and its refutation. Al-Salihi argues that if power and knowledge cannot exist except in a living being, then God would be unable to create them in something unless He first creates life, making life a prerequisite and thus a limitation on God—like a tool. The author refutes this by analogy: just as God is not described as having power to create a substance without an accident (because a substance cannot exist without an accident), nor to create an accident except in a substance, nor to create contact in one body without creating another contact in another body, these are all impossible by their nature. Similarly, the idea that power and knowledge require life is not a limitation on God but a necessary order of creation. The refutation shows that the argument fails because it misunderstands the nature of God's power in relation to the created order.

Key Terms
قدرة
علم
حياة
جوهر
عرض
مماسة
آلة

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Requiring life as a prior condition for power and knowledge implies that God is limited or needs a tool.
Correction: The condition is a necessary order of creation, similar to the impossibility of a substance without an accident; it does not limit God's power.

Checkpoint
How does the author refute al-Salihi's claim that if power and knowledge require life, then God would need life as a tool?
A) By pointing out that God creates life instantly.
B) By comparing it to God's inability to create a substance without an accident.
C) By stating that God does not create power or knowledge in non-living things.
D) By arguing that life is not a tool but a condition.

Key Takeaway
The requirement of life for power and knowledge is a necessary order of creation, not a limitation on God's power.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
This lesson argues that logical impossibilities do not limit God’s power. Is there a hidden area in your life where you think God 'cannot' act because of circumstances you consider necessary limitations? Will you repent of that diminished view and trust His absolute power?
?
Al-Salihi’s error was assuming that a condition (life) makes God dependent. Do you sometimes treat God’s commands or the natural order as 'tools' He needs rather than as His wise creation? How would your worship change if you truly saw no hindrance to His will?
?
The author uses analogies from the nature of creation to silence doubt. When you encounter intellectual objections to tawheed, do you actively seek to understand the logical structure of the refutation, or do you brush them aside? Resolve today to study the proofs deeply so your certainty is unshakable.

Establishing the Implications of Life: Knowledge, Power, and Wisdom
Proof that God's knowledge, power, and wisdom are necessary implications of His life.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand why the attributes of knowledge, power, and wisdom are necessarily established for God based on His life, through two logical proofs.

Core Idea
God's life necessarily entails knowledge, power, and wisdom — they are not separate but required implications.

This passage builds on the earlier establishment of God's life to derive further attributes. The author uses two proofs: one from logical necessity (if life exists, its implications must exist) and one from perfection (life is perfection, God is free from deficiency). Together, they solidify the foundational attributes of God.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage and translation
Read the Arabic passage once, then the English translation. Notice the concise style and the two distinct arguments.
The passage is dense; take your time to absorb each phrase.
2
Identify the two proofs
The author presents two proofs. The first uses the logical relationship between a necessary (life) and its necessary implication (knowledge, power, wisdom). The second uses the concept of perfection and deficiency. Identify each proof in the text.
The first proof is based on the principle: actualization of a necessary without its necessary implication is impossible.
3
Reflect on the logical principle
Consider why the author uses the term 'ملزوم' (necessary) and 'لازم' (necessary implication). Understanding this relationship is key to many theological arguments. Ask yourself: Why can't life exist without its implications?
This principle is foundational in Islamic theology for deriving attributes.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وتحقيق ما ذكر أن ملزومات الحياة من العلم والقدرة والحكمة ثابتة لله تعالى وتحقق الملزوم بدون تحقيق اللازم محال فتحقق الملزوم يستلزم تحقيق اللازم. ودليل آخر أن الحياة صفة كمال ونقيضها نقص وإن الله تعالى منزه عن النقائص.
And the verification of what was mentioned is that the implications of life—knowledge, power, and wisdom—are established for God Almighty, and the actualization of the necessary (life) without the actualization of the necessary implication is impossible; thus, the actualization of the necessary necessitates the actualization of the necessary implication. And another proof: life is a quality of perfection and its opposite is deficiency, and God Almighty is free from deficiencies.
Source pages p. 360

Commentary
This passage is a proof that based on the previously established points, the attributes that are implications of life—knowledge, power, and wisdom—are established for God. The author uses a logical principle: if a necessary (the life of God) is actualized, then what is necessitated by it (the implications) must also be actualized, otherwise it would be impossible. Then, a second proof is given: life is a perfection, its opposite (death) is a deficiency, and God is free from all deficiencies; therefore, life is established for God, and by the first proof, so are its implications. The passage consolidates the earlier arguments to affirm these divine attributes.

Correction: The passage demonstrates that these attributes are necessary implications of life. Without life, they could not exist; they are logically dependent on life.

Checkpoint

A) Because they are mentioned in the Quran.
B) Because they are implications of life, and God's life is actualized.
C) Because life is a perfection and God is perfect.

Key Takeaway
God's life necessarily entails His knowledge, power, and wisdom, and this is confirmed by the perfection of life and God's freedom from deficiency.

?
Life is a quality of perfection; its opposite is deficiency. You bear the soul that God breathed into you. In what areas of your life are you living as if deficiency is acceptable? Are you pursuing the knowledge, power, and wisdom that reflect His perfection? What step will you take today to grow in one of these?
?
The passage proves that God cannot lack knowledge, power, or wisdom. But do you live as if He lacks them? Think of a recent moment when you acted as though God didn't know your situation, couldn't change it, or didn't have a good plan. Confess that to Him now and commit to relying on His attributes.

How God Creates Accidents Without Their Opposites
A concluding rule on how God creates accidents without their opposites, with examples and a note on punishment of the grave.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the Maturidi principle that when God creates an accident in a locus, He does not create any of its opposites simultaneously, and how this applies to knowledge, life, and other attributes.

Core Idea
God never creates opposites together in the same locus.

This passage establishes a key theological rule about divine creation: when God brings an accident into existence in a created being, He does not also create its opposite. The rule is illustrated with examples from sensory qualities and intellectual attributes. Understanding this principle helps clarify the relationship between attributes like knowledge and life, and it also sets the stage for later discussions about the punishment of the grave.

Guided Path
1
Read the Arabic passage
Read the Arabic text once to get the flow. Then read the translation. Notice the logical structure: rule, example, application.
The passage uses 'ثم' (then) to continue from previous discussion.
2
Understand the rule with whiteness
The rule states: when God wants to create an accident (like whiteness), He does not create any of its opposites (like blackness) in the same body.
This is a concrete example to grasp the abstract principle.
3
Apply the rule to knowledge
The same applies to knowledge: God does not create ignorance or death together with knowledge. Instead, He first creates life to repel death, then creates knowledge.
Notice the additional step: life is created to remove the opposite of knowledge (death).
4
Generalize to other attributes
The rule extends to power, hearing, and sight. Each accident is created only when its opposite is absent.
5
Note the theological implications
The passage concludes that knowledge and power are proven by the world, life by a separate indication. It also hints that this does not deny punishment of the grave—a topic for later.
This connects the rule to broader theological arguments.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ثم إن الله تعالى إذا أراد تخليق عرض في محل لا يخلق فيه شيئا من أضداده، كما لو أراد أن يخلق في جسم بياضا لا يخلق فيه شيئا من الألوان المضادة للبياض، وإذا أراد خلق علم لا يخلق فيه الجهل ولا الموت، إذ هما يضادانه، ولا تعري القائم بالذات عن الموت أو الحياة جميعا فيخلق فيه الحياة فيندفع بها الموت الذي هو ضد للعلم فيخلق فيه العلم عند خلو المحل عما يضاد العلم. وكذا في القدرة والسمع والبصر . وإذا عرف هذا فكان العلم والقدرة على هذا المذهب ثابتين بدلالة العالم والحياة ثابتة بدلالة ما هو مدلول العالم، ولن يندفع بهذا جواز عذاب القبر على ما نبين إذا انتهينا إلى تلك المسألة إن شاء الله تعالى - والله الموفق.
Then, when God Almighty wills to create an accident in a locus, He does not create any of its opposites in it—just as if He wills to create whiteness in a body, He does not create any of the colors opposite to whiteness in it. And if He wills to create knowledge, He does not create ignorance or death in it, because they are opposite to it; and the self-subsisting entity is not devoid of death or life altogether, so He creates life in it, and thereby repels death which is opposite to knowledge, and then creates knowledge in it when the locus is free of what opposes knowledge. And likewise for power, hearing, and sight. And when this is known, then knowledge and power according to this doctrine are established by the indication of the world, and life is established by the indication of what is indicated by the world. And this does not negate the possibility of punishment of the grave, as we will explain when we reach that question, God willing. And God is the Granter of success.
Source pages p. 361

Commentary
This passage provides a general rule for how God creates accidents (attributes) in a locus without creating their opposites. Using examples: when creating whiteness, He does not create other colors opposite to whiteness; when creating knowledge, He does not create ignorance or death. Since a self-subsisting entity (like a created being) cannot be simultaneously free of both life and death, God first creates life in it to repel death, and then creates knowledge when the locus is free from its opposite. The same applies to power, hearing, and sight. The author then notes that from this theological doctrine, knowledge and power are proven through the evidence of the created world, while life is proven through its own evidence. Finally, the author hints that this reasoning does not rule out the possibility of punishment in the grave, which will be addressed later. The passage ties together the earlier discussions on attributes and indicates future topics.

Key Terms
عرض
محل
ضد
علم
جهل
موت
حياة
قدرة
سمع
بصر
عذاب القبر

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some may think that God creates knowledge directly without any preparatory creation, or that life and knowledge are always created simultaneously.
Correction: The passage shows that God first creates life to remove the opposite of knowledge (death), and only then creates knowledge in a locus free from death.

Checkpoint
According to the passage, what does God do when He wants to create knowledge in a self-subsisting entity?
A) He creates ignorance simultaneously.
B) He creates life first to repel death, then knowledge.
C) He creates knowledge directly without preconditions.
D) He removes all opposites before creating knowledge.

Key Takeaway
God does not create an accident and its opposite together; when creating knowledge, He first creates life to remove the opposing death.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
The passage shows that God meticulously ensures no opposites coexist in His creation. Think of a struggle in your own life where you feel two opposing desires or thoughts pulling you apart. How does this principle of God's orderly creation challenge you to seek consistency and purity in your intentions? Will you ask God tonight to remove one of those opposites to bring peace?
?
God creates life to repel death before granting knowledge. Have you ever sensed that a period of spiritual 'death'—apathy or sin—was pushed away by a new infusion of life from God, leading to a fresh understanding of faith? What specific step will you take this week to create space for that life?
?
The author affirms that this rule does not negate punishment of the grave. Living in light of that truth, what comfort or fear does it bring you? Are you prepared to meet God now? If not, what is one concrete action you will take today to change that?

God Does Not Create Opposite Accidents Simultaneously
The rule and examples of God not creating opposites simultaneously.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the principle that when God wills to create an accident, He does not create any of its opposites in the same substrate, and see examples of this rule.

Core Idea
God's creative will avoids logical contradictions: opposites never coexist.

This passage establishes a foundational rule in Islamic theology: God does not create two opposite accidents in the same place at once. The author explains this with clear examples, such as whiteness and blackness in a body, or knowledge and ignorance. Understanding this principle helps us grasp how God's attributes are not contradictory.

Guided Path
1
Read the rule
Read the opening sentence: when God wills to create an accident, He does not create any of its opposites. This is the main rule.
Focus on the phrase 'لا يخلق فيه شيئا من أضداده'.
2
Examine the first example
The author gives the example of whiteness: if God wills whiteness in a body, He does not create any opposite color like blackness.
3
Examine the second example
The example of knowledge: if God wills knowledge, He does not create ignorance or death, because they oppose knowledge.
Notice how death is considered opposite to knowledge.
4
Understand the mechanism
The passage explains that life is created to repel death, and then knowledge is created when the place is empty of its opposites.
This shows a sequence: first life, then knowledge.
5
Apply the analogy
The same rule applies to power, hearing, and sight. Reflect on how this principle is universal for all accidents.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ثم إن الله تعالى إذا أراد تخليق عرض في محل لا يخلق فيه شيئا من أضداده، كما لو أراد أن يخلق في جسم بياضا لا يخلق فيه شيئا من الألوان المضادة للبياض، وإذا أراد خلق علم لا يخلق فيه الجهل ولا الموت، إذ هما يضادانه، ولا تعري القائم بالذات عن الموت أو الحياة جميعا فيخلق فيه الحياة فيندفع بها الموت الذي هو ضد للعلم فيخلق فيه العلم عند خلو المحل عما يضاد العلم. وكذا في القدرة والسمع والبصر. وإذا عرف هذا فكان العلم والقدرة على هذا المذهب ثابتين بدلالة العالم والحياة ثابتة بدلالة ما هو مدلول العالم، ولن يندفع بهذا جواز عذاب القبر على ما نبين إذا انتهينا إلى تلك المسألة. والله الموفق.
Then, indeed, if God Almighty wills to create an accident in a place, He does not create in it anything from among its opposites. For example, if He wills to create whiteness in a body, He does not create in it anything from the colors opposite to whiteness. And if He wills to create knowledge, He does not create in it ignorance nor death, since they oppose it. And the self-subsisting entity is not devoid of death or life altogether, so He creates in it life, and thereby death—which is opposite to knowledge—is repelled, and He creates in it knowledge when the place is empty of what opposes knowledge. And likewise in power, hearing, and sight. And when this is known, then knowledge and power according to this doctrine are established by the evidence of the world, and life is established by the evidence of what is the signification of the world. And the permissibility of the punishment of the grave will not be repelled by this, as we will explain when we reach that issue. And God is the Grantor of success.
Source pages p. 361

Commentary
This passage is an explanation of how God's creation of accidents relates to their opposites and serves as evidence for divine attributes. The author states that when God wills to create an accident in a substrate, He does not create any of its opposites simultaneously. For instance, if He wills whiteness, He does not create blackness. Similarly, if He wills knowledge, He does not create ignorance or death, as they are opposites. The self-subsisting entity (al-qā'imu bi-dh-dhāt) is not void of life and death, so God creates life, which repels death, and then creates knowledge when the substrate is free of its opposite. This pattern holds for power, hearing, and sight. Knowing this, knowledge and power are established by the evidence of the world (al-'ālam), and life is established by what is indicated by the world. However, the author notes that this reasoning does not negate the possibility of punishment in the grave, which will be addressed later.

Key Terms
عرض (accident)
ضد (opposite)
علم (knowledge)
حياة (life)

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: One might think that God can create opposite accidents simultaneously without contradiction.
Correction: The passage asserts that God does not create opposites together in the same place, due to logical necessity.

Checkpoint

B) He creates death first to make room for knowledge
C) He creates life to repel death, then creates knowledge

Key Takeaway
God never creates two opposites simultaneously, ensuring logical consistency in His creation.

Establishing Divine Attributes through the Absence of Opposites
Drawing conclusions about divine attributes from the rule about opposites.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how the principle of not creating opposites simultaneously serves as evidence for God's attributes of knowledge, power, and life, and that this does not conflict with the punishment of the grave.

Core Idea
The absence of opposites in creation points to God's perfect attributes.

Having established the rule about opposites, the author now uses it to argue for the reality of divine attributes. He states that knowledge and power are proven by the evidence of the world, and life is proven by what the world indicates. He also acknowledges a potential objection about the punishment of the grave and promises to address it later.

Guided Path
1
Read the conclusion

There is a textual variance: 'بدلالة العالم' vs 'بدلالة العلم'.
3
Understand proof for life
Life is established by the evidence of what is the signification of the world (مدلول العالم). This is a bit complex; it means that since the world is a sign of something, that something (the Creator) must possess life.
4
Address the objection
The author anticipates an objection about the punishment of the grave. He says this reasoning does not negate it and will be explained later.
This shows the author is thorough and aware of potential counterarguments.

Divine Attributes: Real, Not Metaphorical
The author affirms divine attributes as real and refutes deniers.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand that describing Allah with attributes like life, knowledge, and power is literal and real, and why the objections of philosophers and the Batiniyya are invalid.

Core Idea
Divine attributes are real descriptions of God, not mere metaphors.

In this passage, Imam al-Nasafi establishes a crucial theological principle: the attributes we affirm for God are not just figurative expressions but true descriptions of His essence. He also refutes those who claim that applying such terms to God implies similarity with creation, a charge made by philosophers and the Batiniyya Qaramita.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage and note the attributes listed
Read the Arabic passage once to see the full list of attributes: living, knowing, powerful, hearing, seeing. Then read the translation.
These attributes are the direct objects of discussion.
2
Identify the two opposing views
The passage mentions those who claim applying such names to God is impermissible (philosophers and Batiniyya) and those who say the description is metaphorical. Notice how the author positions himself.
The author firmly sides with the view that the description is real.
3
Understand the refutation
The author dismisses the opposing views as corrupt and refers to previous chapters for their refutation. This shows a cumulative argument across the text.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وإذا عرف أنه تعالى حي عالم قادر سميع بصير. نقول: إنه يجوز أن يوصف بها فنقول: هو حي قادر عالم سميع بصير. وزعم بعض المنتسبين إلى الفلسفة كل اسم يجوز إطلاقه على المحدث لا يجوز إطلاقه على أدلة تعالى، لأنه يوجب التشابه وتبعهم على هذا الرأي الفاسد الباطنية القرامطة - لعنهم الله. وقد مر ما يظهر إبطال هذا القول. ثم الوصف له بهذه الصفات حقيقة لا مجاز، وزعم الناس أن الوصف له بهذه الصفات مجاز على إحدى الروايتين عنه. وقد مر الكلام فيه في فصل نفي التشبيه بحمد الله تعالى.
And when it is known that He Almighty is living, knowing, powerful, hearing, seeing. We say: It is permissible to describe Him with them, and we say: He is living, powerful, knowing, hearing, seeing. And some of those affiliated with philosophy claimed that every name whose application to a contingent being is permissible is not permissible to apply to the proofs of Almighty, because it entails similarity. And the Batiniyya Qaramita – may Allah curse them – followed them in this corrupt opinion. And the refutation of this statement has already passed. Then the description of Him with these attributes is real (ḥaqīqa), not metaphorical (majāz). And some people claimed that the description of Him with these attributes is metaphorical according to one of the two narrations from him. And the discussion about it passed in the chapter on negating anthropomorphism (tashbīh), by the praise of God Almighty.
Source pages p. 362

Commentary
This passage is a definitional and refutational statement about divine attributes. The author first establishes that God is known to be living, knowing, powerful, hearing, and seeing, and that it is permissible to describe Him with these attributes. He then critiques philosophers and the Batiniyya Qaramita who claim that names applied to contingent beings should not be applied to God because it implies similarity; the author dismisses this as corrupt and notes that its refutation has already been given. Next, he affirms that the description of God with these attributes is real (ḥaqīqa), not metaphorical (majāz). He mentions that some people hold the view of metaphorical description based on one of two reports from them, but this has already been addressed in a previous chapter on negating anthropomorphism.

Key Terms
حقيقة (real)
مجاز (metaphorical)
تشابه (similarity)
باطنية (Batiniyya)
قرامطة (Qaramita)

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some think that calling God 'knowing' or 'powerful' is merely metaphorical because these terms are used for creation.
Correction: The passage asserts that the description of God with these attributes is real (ḥaqīqa), not metaphorical (majāz), and that the objection based on similarity has been refuted.

Checkpoint
What do the Batiniyya Qaramita claim about applying names to God?
A) It is obligatory
B) It is permissible only metaphorically
C) It is not permissible because it entails similarity with contingent beings
D) It is permissible only for attributes mentioned in the Quran

Key Takeaway
Describing Allah with attributes like life, knowledge, and power is literal and real, not metaphorical, and objections based on supposed similarity have been refuted.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Do you truly believe that Allah's knowledge of you is real, not just a metaphor? If you were to live today with that reality, what would you do differently that you have been avoiding?
?
This passage refutes those who reject describing Allah with certain attributes out of fear of similarity. Is there any attribute of Allah that you feel uncomfortable affirming because it seems too 'human'? Why, and what does that discomfort reveal about your understanding of tawhid?
?
If you fully internalized that Allah's 'hearing' is a real, literal description of Him, would you change what you say in private? What would you whisper to Him right now, knowing He hears you as a real listener?

The Eternity of God's Attributes
The author asserts God's attributes are eternal and refutes those who claim they were created.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand that God's attributes are eternal and essential, and how the Maturidi tradition refutes the view that they are created.

Core Idea
God's attributes are not acquired; they are eternal and essential to His being.

The Maturidi tradition affirms that God's attributes like knowledge and power are eternal, not created. This passage from Imam Nasafi states that clearly and then reports the contrary view of Jahm ibn Safwan and a Shiite group. Understanding this helps you see the key Sunni position on divine attributes.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage and translation
Read the Arabic passage once without analyzing it, then read the English translation. Let the author's own rhythm come through.
Notice the initial assertive tone.
2
Identify the orthodox assertion
The first sentence states that God was described with these attributes in eternity. List the attributes mentioned: life, power, knowledge, hearing, sight.
These attributes are essential, not acquired.
3
Examine Jahm's view on knowledge
Jahm claimed God was not knowing in eternity until He created knowledge. Contrast this with the orthodox view.
This is a key difference.
4
Analyze Jahm's two narrations on power
Jahm gave two contradictory statements: one accepting eternal power, another denying it. Note the inconsistency.
This shows the weakness of his position.
5
Consider the mention of al-Zarariyya
The author adds that a group of Rafida called al-Zarariyya held similar views. Understand why this is relevant.
It broadens the refutation to other deviant groups.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ثم إنه تعالى كان موصوفا بهذه الصفات في الأزل، فكان حيا قادرا عالما سميعا بصيرا. وروي عن جهم بن صفوان الترمذي أنه كان يقول: إن الله تعالى لم يكن في الأزل عالما حتى خلق لنفسه علما فصار عالما، وفي القدرة عنه روايتان: في رواية قال: إنه كان موصوفا بها في الأزل، وقال في رواية: لم يكن حتى خلق لنفسه قدرة. وحكي عن جماعة من الروافض يقال لهم الزرارية.
Then, indeed, He Almighty was described with these attributes in eternity (al-azal), so He was living, powerful, knowing, hearing, seeing. And it is narrated from Jahm ibn Ṣafwān al-Tirmidhī that he used to say: 'God Almighty was not knowing in eternity until He created for Himself knowledge, then He became knowing.' And regarding power, there are two narrations from him: in one narration he said that He was described with it in eternity, and in another narration he said: 'He was not [having power] until He created for Himself power.' And it is reported from a group of the Rafiḍa called al-Zarāriyya.
Source pages p. 362

Commentary
This passage is a doctrinal assertion and refutation regarding the eternity of God's attributes. The author begins by stating that God Almighty was described with these attributes in eternity (al-azal); He was always living, powerful, knowing, hearing, seeing. He then reports the deviant opinion of Jahm ibn Ṣafwān al-Tirmidhī, who held that God was not knowing in eternity but created knowledge for Himself and thus became knowing. Regarding power, Jahm has two conflicting narrations: one stating God was described with power in eternity, another claiming He lacked power until He created it for Himself. The author also mentions a group from the Rafida (a derogatory term for certain Shia) called al-Zarāriyya, who held similar views. The passage thus affirms the orthodox Maturidi position of eternal attributes against these sects.

جهم بن صفوان (Jahm ibn Safwan)
زرارية (Zarariyya)
رافضة (Rafida)
قدرة (power)

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: That God's attributes like knowledge and power were created at some point in time.
Correction: The passage affirms that God was always described with these attributes in eternity; they are essential and not acquired.

Checkpoint

B) God created knowledge for Himself and then became knowing

Key Takeaway
God's attributes are eternal and not created; this passage asserts that and refutes the view of Jahm and the Zarariyya.

Affirming Divine Attributes as Real and Eternal
Nasafi affirms divine attributes as real and eternal.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand that describing Allah with attributes like Life, Knowledge, Power, Hearing, and Sight is real (haqiqa) and that these attributes are eternal (azali).

Core Idea
Divine attributes are real descriptions, not mere metaphors.

In this passage, Imam al-Nasafi establishes the foundational Sunni position on divine attributes. He affirms that Allah has always been described with these attributes and that this description is literal, not figurative. This sets the stage for refuting those who deny the reality or eternity of attributes.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage
Read the Arabic passage once without analysis, then the translation.
2
Identify the two key affirmations
The passage affirms that attributes are real (haqiqa) and eternal (azali). Find the sentences that state each.
3
Reflect on the refuted view
Notice that the passage mentions a philosophical objection and a metaphorical interpretation; it rejects both.
These are referenced but not fully detailed here.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وإذا عرف أنه تعالى حي عالم قادر سميع بصير. نقول: إنه يجوز أن يوصف بها فنقول: هو حي قادر عالم سميع بصير. وزعم بعض المنتسبين إلى الفلسفة كل اسم يجوز إطلاقه على المحدث لا يجوز إطلاقه على أدلة تعالى، لأنه يوجب التشابه وتبعهم على هذا الرأي الفاسد الباطنية القرامطة لعنهم الله. وقد مر ما يظهر إبطال هذا القول. ثم الوصف له بهذه الصفات حقيقة لا مجاز، وزعم الناس أن الوصف له بهذه الصفات مجاز على إحدى الروايتين عنه. وقد مر الكلام فيه في فصل نفي التشبيه بحمد الله تعالى. ثم إنه تعالى كان موصوفا بهذه الصفات في الأزل، فكان حيا قادرا عالما سميعا بصيرا. وروي عن جهم بن صفوان الترمذي أنه كان يقول : إن الله تعالى لم يكن في الأزل عالما حتى خلق لنفسه علما فصار عالما، وفي القدرة عنه روايتان: في رواية قال : إنه كان موصوفا بها في الأزل، وقال في رواية: لم يكن حتى خلق لنفسه قدرة. وحكي عن جماعة من الروافض يقال لهم الزرارية، وهم أصحاب زرارة بن أعين، أن الله تعالى لم يكن عالما سميعا بصيرا حتى خلق لنفسه علما وسمعا وبصرا.
And when it is known that He, exalted, is Living, Knowing, Powerful, Hearing, Seeing. We say: It is permissible to describe Him with them, so we say: He is Living, Powerful, Knowing, Hearing, Seeing. And some of those attributed to philosophy claimed that every name that is permissible to apply to a created thing is not permissible to apply to [?] exalted, because it necessitates similarity, and the Batiniyya Qaramita followed them in this corrupt opinion - may Allah curse them. And the refutation of this statement has already passed. Then the description of Him with these attributes is real, not metaphorical, and some people claimed that the description of Him with these attributes is metaphorical according to one of the two narrations from him. And the discussion about it has already passed in the chapter on negation of tashbih (anthropomorphism), praise be to Allah. Then, exalted, He was described with these attributes in pre-eternity, so He was Living, Powerful, Knowing, Hearing, Seeing. And it is narrated from Jahm ibn Safwan al-Tirmidhi that he used to say: Allah was not Knowing in pre-eternity until He created knowledge for Himself and became Knowing, and regarding power there are two narrations from him: in one narration he said: He was described with it in pre-eternity, and in another narration he said: He was not until He created power for Himself. And it is narrated from a group of the Rawafid called al-Zarariyya, and they are the companions of Zurarah ibn A'yan, that Allah was not Knowing, Hearing, Seeing until He created for Himself knowledge, hearing, and sight.
Source pages p. 362

Commentary
This passage defines the orthodox position on divine attributes and reports heretical views. It begins by stating what is known about Allah: He is Living, Knowing, Powerful, Hearing, Seeing. It affirms that it is permissible to describe Him with these attributes. Then it refutes the claim of some philosophers and the Qaramita that names used for creatures cannot be used for Allah, as this would imply similarity (tashbih). The refutation is referenced as having been given earlier. Next, it asserts that describing Allah with these attributes is real (haqiqa), not metaphorical (majaz), contradicting those who claim it is metaphorical according to one of two narrations. It then affirms that Allah was described with these attributes in pre-eternity (al-azal). The passage then reports two deviant views: 1) Jahm ibn Safwan claimed that Allah was not Knowing in pre-eternity until He created knowledge, and similarly for power in one narration, though another narration from Jahm says He was always powerful. 2) The Zarariyya (followers of Zurarah ibn A'yan) claimed that Allah was not Knowing, Hearing, or Seeing until He created these faculties for Himself. Thus, the passage sets the stage for the refutation that follows.

Key Terms
صفات
حقيقة
مجاز
الأزل

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some think that describing Allah with attributes is metaphorical.
Correction: The passage explicitly states that the description is real (haqiqa), not metaphorical (majaz).

Checkpoint
According to Nasafi, how are Allah's attributes described?
A) As metaphorical (majaz)
B) As real (haqiqa)
C) As neither real nor metaphorical
D) As both real and metaphorical

Key Takeaway
Allah's attributes are real descriptions, not metaphors, and they are eternal.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?

Refuting the Heretical Views of Jahm and Zarariyya
Nasafi reports the temporalist views of Jahm and Zarariyya.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the deviant positions of Jahm ibn Safwan and the Zarariyya regarding the temporal origination of Allah's attributes.

Core Idea
Deviant sects claimed Allah acquired His attributes after not having them.

After affirming the reality and eternity of attributes, al-Nasafi reports two heretical views that deny the eternity of attributes. Jahm ibn Safwan claimed Allah was not Knowing until He created knowledge, and the Zarariyya claimed He was not Knowing, Hearing, or Seeing until He created these faculties. These views are rejected by Sunni orthodoxy.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage
Read the Arabic and translation to understand the reported views.
2
Identify Jahm's position
Jahm said Allah was not Knowing until He created knowledge; note the two narrations on power.
3
Identify Zarariyya's position
The Zarariyya said Allah was not Knowing, Hearing, or Seeing until He created these.
This is a more extreme position than Jahm's.

The Infinite Regress Refutation of Jahm
Nasafi quotes Jahm then refutes with infinite regress argument.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand Jahm's argument against eternal attributes and Nasafi's refutation based on infinite regress and the impossibility of creation without power.

Core Idea
Eternal attributes do not imply multiple eternals; denying them leads to absurd infinite regress.

Jahm ibn Safwan argued that affirming eternal attributes like knowledge and power in Allah would imply multiple eternal entities besides Allah, which he considered shirk. Nasafi begins his refutation by presenting Jahm's position and then dismantling it with a logical dilemma: either power is created by another power (leading to infinite regress) or created without power (impossible). This lesson unpacks that first critical argument.

Guided Path
1
Read Jahm's position
Read the first part of the passage where Jahm's argument is quoted. Notice his reasoning: if Allah were knowing and powerful, He must have knowledge and power distinct from His essence, which would be eternal other-than-Allah.
Jahm's argument hinges on the idea that attributes are distinct from the essence.
2
Understand the dilemma
Nasafi presents a dilemma: if power is created by power, we have infinite regress; if without power, it's impossible. Identify both horns of the dilemma in the text.
3
Reflect on the impossibility
Consider why creating without power is impossible: an entity without the attribute of power cannot produce a powerful effect. This leads to absurdity if allowed for one thing.
This is a foundational principle in kalam: a cause must possess what it gives.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وحكي عن جهم أنه كان يقول : لو كان عالما قادرا في الأزل لكان عالما وقادرا بقدرة وعلم لاستحالة وصف ما لا علم له ولا قدرة بأنه قادر عالم ولا وجه إلى إثبات العلم والقدرة في الأزل، لأنهما يغايران الذات، والقول بقدم غير الله محال. وهذا فاسد، لأنه تعالى لو خلق القدرة بالقدرة لكان الكلام في القدرة الثانية على هذا أيضا وكذا في الثالثة والرابعة إلى ما لا يتناهى . ولو خلقها لا بقدرة فهو محال ، لأن إيجاد من لا قدرة له معنى من المعاني محال، ولو جاز ذا في شيء لجاز في العالم بأسره وهذا باطل. ولأن الفاعل لا عن قدرة مضطر والاضطرار ينافي القدم على ما مر وكذا لو جاز تخليق العلم مع أنه نفسه محكم متقن بلا علم لجاز تخليق جميع العالم، وما فيه من العجائب والبدائع بلا علم وهو محال على ما مر. ولأنه لو خلق العلم قبل القدرة فتخليقه بلا قدرة محال، ولو خلق القدرة قبل العلم فتخليقها مع إحكامها بلا علم محال. ولأنه إذا كان في الأزل لا يعلم نفسه، ولا العلم ولا القدرة والفعل ولا التخليق، ولا يتصور منه تخليق العلم والقدرة لنفسه، ولأنه لو خلق العلم والقدرة إما أن كان خلقهما في ذاته وهو محال ، لأن ذاته ليس بمحل للحوادث، لما في كونه
And it is narrated from Jahm that he used to say: If He were Knowing and Powerful in pre-eternity, then He would be Knowing and Powerful by power and knowledge because it is impossible to describe what has no knowledge and no power as being powerful and knowing, and there is no way to affirm knowledge and power in pre-eternity because they are other than the Essence, and saying that something other than Allah is eternal is impossible. This is corrupt, because if He created power by power, then the same discussion would apply to the second power, and likewise to the third and fourth ad infinitum. And if He created it without power, it is impossible, because bringing into existence one who has no power for a meaning of meanings is impossible, and if this were allowed for something, it would be allowed for the entire world, and this is false. And because the agent without power is compelled, and compulsion contradicts pre-eternity as has passed. And likewise if the creation of knowledge were allowed, despite that it is itself well-ordered and perfected without knowledge, then the creation of the entire world would be allowed, and what is in it of marvels and wonders without knowledge, and this is impossible as has passed. And because if He created knowledge before power, its creation without power is impossible, and if He created power before knowledge, its creation with its perfection without knowledge is impossible. And because when He is in pre-eternity not knowing Himself, nor knowledge nor power nor action nor creation, then creation of knowledge and power for Himself is not conceivable. And because if He created knowledge and power, either He created them in His Essence, and this is impossible because His Essence is not a locus for accidents, because in its being...
Source pages p. 363

Commentary
This passage presents a detailed refutation of Jahm ibn Safwan's position that Allah cannot have eternal attributes. It begins by quoting Jahm's argument: if Allah were knowing and powerful in pre-eternity, He would have knowledge and power distinct from His essence, implying multiple eternal entities, which is impossible. Nasafi then refutes this with several arguments: 1) If power were created by another power, an infinite regress (tasalsul) results. 2) If power were created without any power, it is impossible for an entity without power to produce a power. 3) An agent without power is compelled, and compulsion contradicts pre-eternity. 4) If knowledge could be created without pre-existing knowledge, then the entire well-ordered world could be created without knowledge, which is absurd. 5) If knowledge were created before power, its creation without power is impossible; if power before knowledge, its creation without knowledge is impossible. 6) In pre-eternity, if Allah did not know Himself, He could not create knowledge for Himself. 7) If knowledge and power were created in His essence, that is impossible because His essence is not a locus for accidents (mahall lil-hawadith). The refutation is cut off at the last point but demonstrates the impossibility of Jahm's view through logical contradictions.

Key Terms
جهم
التسلسل
القدرة
الذات

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some think that denying eternal attributes avoids shirk by keeping Allah simple.
Correction: This passage shows that denying attributes leads to logical absurdities (infinite regress or impossibility), so affirming them is rationally necessary.

Checkpoint
What is the first horn of the dilemma Nasafi presents against Jahm?
A) If power is created by power, there is an infinite regress.
B) If power is not created, Allah is powerless.
C) If power is created without power, it is possible.
D) If power is eternal, it is a second god.

Key Takeaway
Nasafi refutes Jahm by showing that denying eternal attributes forces an impossible choice between infinite regress and creation without power.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you think about Allah's attributes like knowledge and power, do you have any hidden fear that affirming them fully might somehow compromise His oneness? Examine your heart: are you more comfortable limiting Him to avoid a perceived risk, even if it means falling into logical absurdity like Jahm?
?
This lesson shows that denying eternal attributes leads to infinite regress or impossibility. Are there any beliefs you hold about Allah that you have not thought through logically, because you were afraid of where the logic might lead? Will you commit to reasoning through your faith carefully, trusting that truth will never contradict sound reasoning?
?
Jahm's mistake was to assume that attributes being 'other than the Essence' means they are separate gods. Have you ever reduced Allah's attributes to mere names, stripping them of their reality, out of a misplaced sense of caution? What would change in your worship if you truly believed that Allah's knowledge and power are real and eternal, without falling into shirk?

Compulsion, Knowledge, and the Locus of Accidents
Nasafi presents three additional refutations: compulsion, necessity of knowledge, and essence not locus.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand Nasafi's further arguments against Jahm: the necessity of power to avoid compulsion, the need for knowledge to produce order, and the impossibility of attributes inhering in Allah's essence.

Core Idea
Without eternal attributes, Allah would be compelled and creation would lack order, which is impossible.

After refuting Jahm with the infinite regress argument, Nasafi continues with three more decisive points. First, an agent without power is compelled (mudtar), which contradicts Allah's eternal sovereignty. Second, the perfect order of creation proves it cannot arise without knowledge. Third, if attributes were created within Allah's essence, that essence would become a locus for accidents—impossible for the Eternal. This lesson unpacks these deeper theological principles.

Guided Path
1
Understand the compulsion argument
Read the passage starting from 'ولأن الفاعل لا عن قدرة مضطر'. Nasafi argues that an agent without power is compelled, and compulsion is incompatible with pre-eternity (qidam).
This argument links power to voluntary agency.
2
Analyze the knowledge argument
The next argument: if the well-ordered world could be created without knowledge, then all marvels could be created without knowledge, which is false. Nasafi uses the observed order to prove the necessity of divine knowledge.
3
Examine the locus argument
The final portion argues that attributes cannot be created in Allah's essence because that would make His essence a locus for accidents (hawadith), which is impossible for the Eternal.
This is a key Ash'ari/Maturidi principle: the Eternal does not undergo change.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وحكي عن جهم أنه كان يقول : لو كان عالما قادرا في الأزل لكان عالما وقادرا بقدرة وعلم لاستحالة وصف ما لا علم له ولا قدرة بأنه قادر عالم ولا وجه إلى إثبات العلم والقدرة في الأزل، لأنهما يغايران الذات، والقول بقدم غير الله محال. وهذا فاسد، لأنه تعالى لو خلق القدرة بالقدرة لكان الكلام في القدرة الثانية على هذا أيضا وكذا في الثالثة والرابعة إلى ما لا يتناهى . ولو خلقها لا بقدرة فهو محال ، لأن إيجاد من لا قدرة له معنى من المعاني محال، ولو جاز ذا في شيء لجاز في العالم بأسره وهذا باطل. ولأن الفاعل لا عن قدرة مضطر والاضطرار ينافي القدم على ما مر وكذا لو جاز تخليق العلم مع أنه نفسه محكم متقن بلا علم لجاز تخليق جميع العالم، وما فيه من العجائب والبدائع بلا علم وهو محال على ما مر. ولأنه لو خلق العلم قبل القدرة فتخليقه بلا قدرة محال، ولو خلق القدرة قبل العلم فتخليقها مع إحكامها بلا علم محال. ولأنه إذا كان في الأزل لا يعلم نفسه، ولا العلم ولا القدرة والفعل ولا التخليق، ولا يتصور منه تخليق العلم والقدرة لنفسه، ولأنه لو خلق العلم والقدرة إما أن كان خلقهما في ذاته وهو محال ، لأن ذاته ليس بمحل للحوادث، لما في كونه
And it is narrated from Jahm that he used to say: If He were Knowing and Powerful in pre-eternity, then He would be Knowing and Powerful by power and knowledge because it is impossible to describe what has no knowledge and no power as being powerful and knowing, and there is no way to affirm knowledge and power in pre-eternity because they are other than the Essence, and saying that something other than Allah is eternal is impossible. This is corrupt, because if He created power by power, then the same discussion would apply to the second power, and likewise to the third and fourth ad infinitum. And if He created it without power, it is impossible, because bringing into existence one who has no power for a meaning of meanings is impossible, and if this were allowed for something, it would be allowed for the entire world, and this is false. And because the agent without power is compelled, and compulsion contradicts pre-eternity as has passed. And likewise if the creation of knowledge were allowed, despite that it is itself well-ordered and perfected without knowledge, then the creation of the entire world would be allowed, and what is in it of marvels and wonders without knowledge, and this is impossible as has passed. And because if He created knowledge before power, its creation without power is impossible, and if He created power before knowledge, its creation with its perfection without knowledge is impossible. And because when He is in pre-eternity not knowing Himself, nor knowledge nor power nor action nor creation, then creation of knowledge and power for Himself is not conceivable. And because if He created knowledge and power, either He created them in His Essence, and this is impossible because His Essence is not a locus for accidents, because in its being...
Source pages p. 363

Commentary
This passage presents a detailed refutation of Jahm ibn Safwan's position that Allah cannot have eternal attributes. It begins by quoting Jahm's argument: if Allah were knowing and powerful in pre-eternity, He would have knowledge and power distinct from His essence, implying multiple eternal entities, which is impossible. Nasafi then refutes this with several arguments: 1) If power were created by another power, an infinite regress (tasalsul) results. 2) If power were created without any power, it is impossible for an entity without power to produce a power. 3) An agent without power is compelled, and compulsion contradicts pre-eternity. 4) If knowledge could be created without pre-existing knowledge, then the entire well-ordered world could be created without knowledge, which is absurd. 5) If knowledge were created before power, its creation without power is impossible; if power before knowledge, its creation without knowledge is impossible. 6) In pre-eternity, if Allah did not know Himself, He could not create knowledge for Himself. 7) If knowledge and power were created in His essence, that is impossible because His essence is not a locus for accidents (mahall lil-hawadith). The refutation is cut off at the last point but demonstrates the impossibility of Jahm's view through logical contradictions.

Key Terms
المضطر
العلم
المحل للحوادث

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some think that if Allah creates attributes within Himself, He remains transcendent.
Correction: Nasafi argues that creating attributes in the essence would make it a locus for accidents, which contradicts divine immutability.

Checkpoint
What does Nasafi argue about an agent without power?
A) He is free.
B) He is compelled.
C) He is eternal.
D) He is knowledgeable.

Key Takeaway
Without eternal attributes, Allah would be compelled, creation would lack order, and His essence would become a locus for change—all impossible.

?
The lesson shows that denying Allah's attributes leads to absurd contradictions. Have I ever, even unknowingly, held a view about Allah that, if followed to its logical end, would make Him less than He is? What step will I take today to purify my understanding of tawhid?
?
Nasafi argues that Allah's essence cannot be a locus for change. Does this truth make me approach Him with awe and reverence, or have I become casual in my worship? How will I remind myself of His transcendence the next time I pray?
