The Erroneous Views on Divine Attributes
The author reports the views of Zurara and Jahm on divine attributes.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the claims made by Zurara ibn A'yan and Jahm that God's attributes are created in time.

Core Idea
Some early theologians claimed God acquired attributes after creating them.

Before we examine the refutation of the claim that God's attributes are created, we first need to understand exactly what was claimed. The author reports two specific views: that of Zurara ibn A'yan and his followers, and that of Jahm. These views set up the problem that the infinite regress argument solves.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage identifying the two views
Read the Arabic passage once and note the two distinct claims: one from the followers of Zurara, and one from Jahm. The translation will help you see the difference.
Zurara's group said God was not knowing, hearing, seeing until He created those attributes for Himself.
2
Compare the two views
Notice that both views deny that God's attributes are eternal. Zurara says God acquired them later. Jahm argues they cannot be eternal because they are distinct from God's essence.
3
Understand Jahm's reasoning
Jahm argues that if God were knowing and powerful in pre-eternity, He would have to have knowledge and power as distinct entities, but nothing other than God can be eternal. So He cannot be described as knowing in pre-eternity.
This reasoning is based on the principle that attributes are other than the essence.
4
Reflect on why these views are problematic
Consider that if attributes are created, it implies that God was not always perfect, and that He depends on something other than Himself for His attributes.
This will lead into the refutation in the next lesson.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
أصحاب زرارة بن أعين، أن الله تعالى لم يكن عالما سميعا بصيرا حتى خلق لنفسه علما وسمعا وبصرا، وحكي عن جهم أنه كان يقول : لو كان عالما قادرا في الأزل لكان عالما وقادرا بقدرة ،وعلم لاستحالة وصف ما لا علم له ولا قدرة بأنه قادر عالم ولا وجه إلى إثبات العلم والقدرة في الأزل، لأنهما يغايران الذات، والقول بقدم غير الله محال. وهذا فاسد، لأنه تعالى لو خلق القدرة بالقدرة لكان الكلام في القدرة الثانية على هذا أيضا وكذا في الثالثة والرابعة إلى ما لا يتناهى . ولو خلقها لا بقدرة فهو محال ، لأن إيجاد من لا قدرة له معنى من المعاني محال، ولو جاز ذا في شيء لجاز في العالم بأسره وهذا باطل
The followers of Zurara ibn A'yan [held] that God Almighty was not knowing, hearing, seeing until He created for Himself knowledge, hearing, and sight. And it is related from Jahm that he used to say: If He were knowing, powerful in pre-eternity, He would be knowing and powerful by power and knowledge because it is impossible to describe one who has no knowledge or power as powerful or knowing, and there is no way to affirm knowledge and power in pre-eternity because they are distinct from the essence, and affirming the pre-eternity of other than God is impossible. And this is corrupt, because if God Almighty created power by power, then the same discussion would apply to the second power, and likewise to the third and fourth ad infinitum. And if He created it not by power, it is impossible, because bringing into existence something that has no power for a meaning among meanings is impossible, and if this were permissible in anything, it would be permissible in the entire world, and this is false.
Source pages p. 363

Commentary
This passage is a refutation. It first presents the erroneous views of Zurara ibn A'yan and Jahm: that God was not eternally knowing, hearing, seeing, but acquired these attributes later. Jahm argued that if God were knowing and powerful in pre-eternity, He would have power and knowledge as distinct entities, which is impossible because they are other than God and nothing other than God can be pre-eternal. The author then refutes this by pointing out a dilemma: if God created power by another power, that second power would itself require a prior power, leading to an infinite regress. If He created power without any power, that is impossible because an agent without power cannot bring anything into existence. If such an act were possible, it would apply to the whole world, which is absurd.

Key Terms
قدرة
علم
قِدَم

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some think that God's attributes could be created in time without affecting His perfection.
Correction: The passage shows that such a view implies God was imperfect before creating attributes, which contradicts His essential perfection.

Checkpoint
What did the followers of Zurara believe about God's attributes?
A) God always had knowledge, hearing, and sight.
B) God created knowledge, hearing, and sight for Himself after not having them.
C) God's attributes are identical to His essence.
D) God's attributes are completely unknown.

Key Takeaway
The views of Zurara and Jahm both deny the eternity of God's attributes, setting up the need for a refutation.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you describe God as 'All-Knowing,' do you truly believe His knowledge is eternal and perfect, or do you unconsciously imagine it as something He 'acquired' over time? How does this affect your reliance on His guidance?
?
If you were to argue with someone who says 'God cannot have eternal attributes because that would imply multiple eternal beings,' what would you say using the lesson's source? What does your answer reveal about your own understanding of Tawhid?
?
Reflect on a time you doubted that God fully knew your situation. Did you fall into thinking His knowledge is limited or acquired? How will you remind yourself of the truth from this lesson when such doubt creeps in again?

Refutation by Infinite Regress
The author refutes the claim that attributes are created using a logical dilemma.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the infinite regress argument that refutes the claim that God's attributes are created.

Core Idea
Attributing creation to God's attributes leads to an infinite regress or an impossible act.

The author now delivers a powerful refutation of the views just presented. He presents a logical dilemma: either God's power is created by another power, leading to an infinite regress, or it is created without any power, which is impossible. This argument shows that the attributes cannot be created.

Guided Path
1
Read the refutation passage
Read the Arabic passage and its translation carefully. Note that it begins with 'وهذا فاسد' (And this is corrupt), signaling the refutation.
2
Identify the two horns of the dilemma
The author presents two possibilities: (1) God created power by another power, or (2) He created it without any power. Understand why each is impossible.
3
Understand the infinite regress argument
If God created power by another power, then that second power itself would need to be created by a prior power, ad infinitum. This is impossible because an infinite chain of causes cannot exist.
This is a classic infinite regress (تسلسل) argument.
4
Understand the second horn
If God created power without any power, that is impossible because an agent who has no power cannot bring anything into existence. The author adds that if such an act were possible, it would apply to everything, which is absurd.
5
Connect the refutation to the original views
How does this refute Zurara and Jahm? They claimed attributes are created. This dilemma shows that creation of an attribute like power is logically impossible, so the claim is false.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
أصحاب زرارة بن أعين، أن الله تعالى لم يكن عالما سميعا بصيرا حتى خلق لنفسه علما وسمعا وبصرا، وحكي عن جهم أنه كان يقول : لو كان عالما قادرا في الأزل لكان عالما وقادرا بقدرة ،وعلم لاستحالة وصف ما لا علم له ولا قدرة بأنه قادر عالم ولا وجه إلى إثبات العلم والقدرة في الأزل، لأنهما يغايران الذات، والقول بقدم غير الله محال. وهذا فاسد، لأنه تعالى لو خلق القدرة بالقدرة لكان الكلام في القدرة الثانية على هذا أيضا وكذا في الثالثة والرابعة إلى ما لا يتناهى . ولو خلقها لا بقدرة فهو محال ، لأن إيجاد من لا قدرة له معنى من المعاني محال، ولو جاز ذا في شيء لجاز في العالم بأسره وهذا باطل
The followers of Zurara ibn A'yan [held] that God Almighty was not knowing, hearing, seeing until He created for Himself knowledge, hearing, and sight. And it is related from Jahm that he used to say: If He were knowing, powerful in pre-eternity, He would be knowing and powerful by power and knowledge because it is impossible to describe one who has no knowledge or power as powerful or knowing, and there is no way to affirm knowledge and power in pre-eternity because they are distinct from the essence, and affirming the pre-eternity of other than God is impossible. And this is corrupt, because if God Almighty created power by power, then the same discussion would apply to the second power, and likewise to the third and fourth ad infinitum. And if He created it not by power, it is impossible, because bringing into existence something that has no power for a meaning among meanings is impossible, and if this were permissible in anything, it would be permissible in the entire world, and this is false.
Source pages p. 363

Commentary
This passage is a refutation. It first presents the erroneous views of Zurara ibn A'yan and Jahm: that God was not eternally knowing, hearing, seeing, but acquired these attributes later. Jahm argued that if God were knowing and powerful in pre-eternity, He would have power and knowledge as distinct entities, which is impossible because they are other than God and nothing other than God can be pre-eternal. The author then refutes this by pointing out a dilemma: if God created power by another power, that second power would itself require a prior power, leading to an infinite regress. If He created power without any power, that is impossible because an agent without power cannot bring anything into existence. If such an act were possible, it would apply to the whole world, which is absurd.

Key Terms
قدرة
تسلسل
محال

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some think that God's attributes could be created without affecting His nature.
Correction: The infinite regress argument shows that creating even one attribute leads to absurdity, so it is impossible.

Checkpoint

A) God creates power without any power.
B) God creates power by another power.
C) God does not create power at all.
D) Power is eternal.

Key Takeaway
The dilemma shows that creating an attribute like power is logically impossible, refuting the claim that attributes are created.

?

How does the logical impossibility of created attributes deepen your awe of God's eternal power? Will you pause in your next prayer to reflect that His power is not borrowed or contingent?
?
The dilemma shows that any flaw in understanding God's attributes leads to absurdity. Are you willing to examine your own beliefs about God critically, even if it means letting go of comfortable assumptions? What step will you take today to ensure your knowledge of God's attributes is sound?

The Necessity of Power and Knowledge in Creation
Three proofs against createdness of divine knowledge and power

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand three arguments demonstrating that God's knowledge and power cannot be created because an agent without power is compelled, creating knowledge without knowledge is impossible, and power and knowledge must coexist in the Creator.

Core Idea
An agent without power is compelled; creating order requires knowledge.

The author presents three interconnected proofs. The first establishes that an agent without power is compelled, which contradicts divine pre-eternity. The second shows that if knowledge could be created without prior knowledge, then the whole universe could be created without knowledge, which is absurd. The third argues that knowledge and power cannot be created sequentially because each requires the other for its creation.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage and identify the three proofs
Carefully read the Arabic and translation. Look for the three distinct arguments: agent without power, creating knowledge without knowledge, and sequential creation of knowledge and power.
2
Understand the concept of compulsion versus power
Reflect on why an agent without power is compelled and why compulsion negates pre-eternity. This is a key logical foundation.
3
Reflect on the logical ordering of knowledge and power
Consider why creating knowledge before power or power before knowledge is impossible. Both must be present eternally.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ولأن الفاعل لا عن قدرة مضطر والاضطرار ينافي القدم على ما مر وكذا (لو جاز) تخليق العلم مع أنه نفسه محكم متقن بلا علم لجاز تخليق جميع العالم، وما فيه من العجائب والبدائع بلا علم وهو محال على ما مر ، ولأنه لو خلق العلم قبل القدرة فتخليقه بلا قدرة ،محال، ولو خلق القدرة قبل العلم فتخليقها مع إحكامها بلا علم محال . ولأنه إذا كان في الأزل لا يعلم نفسه، ولا العلم ولا القدرة والفعل ولا التخليق، ولا يتصور منه تخليق العلم والقدرة لنفسه، ولأنه لو خلق العلم والقدرة إما أن كان خلقهما في ذاته وهو محال ، لأن ذاته ليس بمحل للحوادث، لما في كونه محل الحوادث دليل حدوثه في نفسه وبقبول الهيولى في الحوادث عند الدهرية استدللنا على كونها حادثة.
And because an agent without power is compelled, and compulsion negates pre-eternity as previously mentioned. Likewise, if it were permissible to create knowledge—while it itself is well-ordered and perfect—without knowledge, then it would be permissible to create the entire world and what is in it of wonders and marvels without knowledge, which is impossible as previously mentioned. And because if He created knowledge before power, then its creation without power is impossible. And if He created power before knowledge, then its creation along with its perfection without knowledge is impossible. And because if in pre-eternity He does not know Himself, nor knowledge, nor power, nor action, nor creation, then it is inconceivable that He should create knowledge and power for Himself. And because if He created knowledge and power, then either He created them in His essence—which is impossible, because His essence is not a locus for accidents, because its being a locus for accidents is proof of its own temporality, and by accepting matter for accidents according to the Dahriyya we have argued that they are temporal.
Source pages p. 363

Commentary
This passage presents multiple additional proofs. The first proof: an agent without power is compelled, and compulsion contradicts pre-eternity. Second: if creating knowledge without prior knowledge were possible, then creating the universe without knowledge would also be possible, which is false. Third: creating knowledge before power is impossible (needs power), and creating power before knowledge is impossible (needs knowledge). Fourth: if in pre-eternity God did not know Himself or anything, He could not create knowledge and power for Himself. Fifth: if He created them in His essence, that is impossible because His essence is not a locus for accidents (being a locus for accidents would make it temporal, as the Dahriyya's argument about matter shows).

Key Terms
قدرة
اضطرار
علم

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some might think God's power could be created after knowledge or vice versa.
Correction: The author argues that sequential creation of knowledge and power is impossible because each requires the other for its own creation.

Checkpoint

A) Creating knowledge before power is impossible.
B) An agent without power is compelled, negating pre-eternity.
C) The universe cannot be created without knowledge.
D) Power and knowledge cannot coexist.

Key Takeaway
God's knowledge and power cannot be created because an agent without power is compelled, creating order requires knowledge, and power and knowledge must coexist eternally.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?

?

?
The proof that power and knowledge cannot be created means God has always been all-powerful and all-knowing. Does your daily prayer life reflect that belief, or do you doubt that He is able to answer? What step will you take today to pray with greater certainty in His uncreated power?

God's Pre-eternal Knowledge and the Impossibility of Accidents in His Essence
Two proofs: pre-eternal knowledge and locus of accidents

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand two arguments that God's knowledge and power are eternal: first, if God did not know Himself in pre-eternity, He could not create knowledge for Himself; second, creating knowledge and power in His essence is impossible because His essence is not a locus for accidents.

Core Idea
God's essence cannot be a locus for accidents.

This passage presents two additional proofs. The first argues that if God did not know Himself or anything in pre-eternity, it is inconceivable that He could create knowledge and power for Himself. The second proof argues that creating knowledge and power in His essence is impossible because His essence is not a locus for accidents; being a locus would imply temporality.

Guided Path
1
Read the two proofs
Read the Arabic and translation. Notice the two distinct arguments: pre-eternal ignorance and the locus of accidents.
2
Understand the argument about pre-eternal ignorance
Consider why God's not knowing Himself in pre-eternity would make it impossible for Him to create knowledge for Himself. Creation requires knowledge.
3
Grasp the principle that God's essence is not a locus for accidents
Reflect on why being a locus for accidents would imply temporality. The Dahriyya argument is referenced.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ولأن الفاعل لا عن قدرة مضطر والاضطرار ينافي القدم على ما مر وكذا (لو جاز) تخليق العلم مع أنه نفسه محكم متقن بلا علم لجاز تخليق جميع العالم، وما فيه من العجائب والبدائع بلا علم وهو محال على ما مر ، ولأنه لو خلق العلم قبل القدرة فتخليقه بلا قدرة ،محال، ولو خلق القدرة قبل العلم فتخليقها مع إحكامها بلا علم محال . ولأنه إذا كان في الأزل لا يعلم نفسه، ولا العلم ولا القدرة والفعل ولا التخليق، ولا يتصور منه تخليق العلم والقدرة لنفسه، ولأنه لو خلق العلم والقدرة إما أن كان خلقهما في ذاته وهو محال ، لأن ذاته ليس بمحل للحوادث، لما في كونه محل الحوادث دليل حدوثه في نفسه وبقبول الهيولى في الحوادث عند الدهرية استدللنا على كونها حادثة.
And because an agent without power is compelled, and compulsion negates pre-eternity as previously mentioned. Likewise, if it were permissible to create knowledge—while it itself is well-ordered and perfect—without knowledge, then it would be permissible to create the entire world and what is in it of wonders and marvels without knowledge, which is impossible as previously mentioned. And because if He created knowledge before power, then its creation without power is impossible. And if He created power before knowledge, then its creation along with its perfection without knowledge is impossible. And because if in pre-eternity He does not know Himself, nor knowledge, nor power, nor action, nor creation, then it is inconceivable that He should create knowledge and power for Himself. And because if He created knowledge and power, then either He created them in His essence—which is impossible, because His essence is not a locus for accidents, because its being a locus for accidents is proof of its own temporality, and by accepting matter for accidents according to the Dahriyya we have argued that they are temporal.
Source pages p. 363

Commentary
This passage presents multiple additional proofs. The first proof: an agent without power is compelled, and compulsion contradicts pre-eternity. Second: if creating knowledge without prior knowledge were possible, then creating the universe without knowledge would also be possible, which is false. Third: creating knowledge before power is impossible (needs power), and creating power before knowledge is impossible (needs knowledge). Fourth: if in pre-eternity God did not know Himself or anything, He could not create knowledge and power for Himself. Fifth: if He created them in His essence, that is impossible because His essence is not a locus for accidents (being a locus for accidents would make it temporal, as the Dahriyya's argument about matter shows).

Correction: The author argues that God's essence cannot be a locus for accidents; thus, attributes like knowledge and power are eternal, not created in Him.

Divine Attributes

7 min
The Impossibility of Creating Attributes in Any Locus
The author examines three possible loci for created attributes and shows each is impossible.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand why it is impossible for God's essential attributes (like knowledge and power) to be created, whether in a locus or not, and how this argument upholds the eternal nature of divine attributes.

Core Idea
If God's attributes were created, they would need a locus—and that locus cannot be God or anything else.

This lesson tackles a foundational argument in Sunni theology: that God's attributes cannot be created. The author examines every conceivable way attributes could be brought into existence and shows each leads to an absurdity. By working through these exhaustive possibilities, you will see why the divine attributes must be eternal, uncreated, and subsisting in God's essence.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage and its translation
Begin by reading the Arabic passage once, then the full translation. Let the author's rigorous reasoning unfold without interruption.
The argument is dense; reading the translation carefully is essential.
2
Identify the three possibilities refuted
The passage classifies three ways God might create attributes: (1) not in a locus, (2) in another locus, (3) before having knowledge and power. List them and notice how each is eliminated.
These correspond to the three 'as for' (وأما) clauses in the Arabic.
3
Understand why attributes cannot exist without a locus
Focus on the first refutation: attributes cannot subsist by themselves. If they could, we would be forced to accept that accidents like motion and color could also exist independently, which is absurd.
This is a key principle in kalam: attributes depend on a subject.
4
Reflect on the conclusion and its implications
After all three possibilities are shown impossible, the author concludes that the original claim—that attributes are created—is impossible. Consider how this argument safeguards the uniqueness of God.
This argument is used later in refuting sects like the Karamiyya and Qadariyya.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وأما إن كان خلقهما لا في محل، وهو محال، لاستحالة قيام الصفات بأنفسها، ولو جاز ذا على العلم والقدرة لجاز على الحركة والسكون والسواد والبياض. ولأنهما لو قاما بأنفسهما لم يكونا بكونهما قدرة وعلما له أولى من كونهما قدرة وعلما لغيره وأما إن خلقهما في محل آخر. وهو محال، لأنه يوجب أن يكون العالم والقادر المحل الذي قاما به لا الله تعالى كما في تخليقه تعالى الحركة والسكون والسواد والبياض في محل، كان المحل هو المتحرك الساكن الأسود الأبيض لا الله تعالى الذي خلقها فكذا هذا. ولأنه إما أن خلق في محل آخر قديم، والقول بقديم قائم بالذات سوى الله تعالى محال على ما مر . وإما أن خلقه في محل لما مر، وإما أن (أحدثه الباري جل وعلا، ومحال أحداثه قبل إحداث علمه وقدرته لما أن) إيجاده بدون القدرة عليه والعلم به محال، وإذا كان القول بإحداثه علمه وقدرته ينقسم إلى هذه الأقسام وهي كلها داخلة في حيز المحال كان محالا في نفسه. ونشرح هذا الكلام بأتم من هذا إذا انتهينا إلى إبطال قول الكرامية – إن الله تعالى محل للحوادث - وإبطال وقول القدرية - إن كلام الله تعالى محدث إن شاء
And as for if He created them not in a locus—it is impossible because of the impossibility of attributes subsisting by themselves. And if this were allowed for knowledge and power, it would be allowed for motion, rest, blackness, and whiteness. And because if they subsisted by themselves, they would not be, by being power and knowledge for Him, any more appropriately power and knowledge for Him than for another. And as for if He created them in another locus—it is impossible because it would require that the knowing and powerful one be the locus in which they subsist, not God Almighty, just as when God Almighty creates motion, rest, blackness, and whiteness in a locus, the locus becomes the moving, resting, black, white entity, not God Almighty who created them. Thus likewise this. And because either He created [them] in another pre-eternal locus—and the statement of a pre-eternal entity subsisting by essence other than God is impossible as previously mentioned—or He created them in a locus as previously [discussed], or that (the Creator, mighty and majestic, brought them into existence, and it is impossible for Him to bring them into existence before bringing into existence His knowledge and power because) bringing into existence without power over it and knowledge of it is impossible. And if the statement about His bringing into existence His knowledge and power divides into these divisions, and they are all within the realm of the impossible, then it is impossible in itself. And we will explain this speech more fully than this when we reach the refutation of the statement of the Karamiyya—that God Almighty is a locus for accidents—and the refutation of the statement of the Qadariyya—that the speech of God Almighty is temporal if He wills.
Source pages p. 364

Commentary
This passage classifies and refutes three hypothetical loci for created attributes. First: if created not in a locus (i.e., subsisting by themselves), this is impossible because attributes cannot subsist independently; if they could, motion and color would also, and then these attributes would not necessarily belong to God. Second: if created in another locus, then that locus would be the knowing and powerful one, not God—like when God creates motion in a body, the body moves, not God. Also, that locus would either be pre-eternal (impossible) or temporal (already covered). Third: the option that God creates them prior to having knowledge and power is impossible because creation requires knowledge and power. Thus all possibilities are impossible, proving that God's attributes cannot be created. The author ends by noting he will discuss the Karamiyya and Qadariyya later in more detail.

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some might think that if God creates attributes in a locus, the locus could be God Himself, reducing Him to a body.
Correction: The argument about locus does not reduce God to a body; it shows that created attributes require a locus, which cannot be God because that would imply change in His essence. Instead, attributes must be eternal and subsist in His essence without a created substrate.

Key Takeaway
God's attributes cannot be created because every possible scenario for their creation leads to an impossibility, proving they must be eternal.

?
The argument shows that God cannot be a locus for temporal attributes. Does your heart ever attribute change or newness to God (e.g., thinking He becomes angry after you sin, rather than His anger being eternal)? What do you need to change in how you conceive of God's attributes?

Impossibility of God Creating His Own Attributes
Proof that divine attributes cannot be created via exhaustive division of possibilities.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand why it is rationally impossible for God to create His own attributes of knowledge and power, based on three refuted possibilities.

Core Idea
God's attributes cannot be created in any way—neither in God, nor in another, nor independently.

This passage presents a rigorous argument against the idea that God could create His own attributes. The author, Imam al-Nasafi, examines all logical possibilities for such a creation and demonstrates that each leads to an impossibility. By working through these possibilities, we see that the very concept is rationally untenable. The argument also sets the stage for refuting specific sectarian views.

Guided Path
1
Identify the three possibilities
Read the passage and note the three ways the author considers for God to create His own knowledge and power: in a locus, not in a locus, or in another locus.
The passage uses a dialectical structure: if x, then y; but y is false, so x is false.
2
Understand the first refutation
The first option (creating in a locus) is rejected because the locus would need to be a body, and bodies are created, leading to circularity. The passage does not elaborate this but implies it from earlier context.
The author references 'the locus of accidents is a proof of its createdness'—meaning any locus for attributes must be a created body.
3
Understand the second refutation
Creating attributes without a locus is impossible because attributes cannot subsist by themselves. If knowledge and power could stand alone, they would be independent substances, which is absurd.
The author compares to physical accidents like motion and color, which also cannot exist without a subject.
4
Understand the third refutation
Creating attributes in another locus would make that locus the knowing and powerful entity, not God. Also, that locus would either be eternal (impossible) or created (leading to regress).
This prevents the idea that God's attributes could be created in a substrate like the Preserved Tablet.
5
Reflect on the conclusion
Since all possibilities are impossible, the assertion that God creates His own knowledge and power is impossible. This refutes the views of the Karramiyya and Qadariyya.
The author promises a fuller explanation later when targeting those sects.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
محل الحوادث دليل حدوثه في نفسه وبقبول الهيولى في الحوادث عند الدهرية استدللنا على كونها حادثة. وأما إن كان خلقهما لا في محل، وهو محال، لاستحالة قيام الصفات بأنفسها، ولو جاز ذا على العلم والقدرة لجاز على الحركة والسكون والسواد والبياض. ولأنهما لو قاما بأنفسهما لم يكونا بكونهما قدرة وعلما له أولى من كونهما قدرة وعلما لغيره وأما إن خلقهما في محل آخر. وهو محال، لأنه يوجب أن يكون العالم والقادر المحل الذي قاما به لا الله تعالى كما في تخليقه تعالى الحركة والسكون والسواد والبياض في محل، كان المحل هو المتحرك الساكن الأسود الأبيض لا الله تعالى الذي خلقها فكذا هذا. ولأنه إما أن خلق في محل آخر قديم، والقول بقديم قائم بالذات سوى الله تعالى محال على ما مر . وإما أن خلقه في محل لما مر، وإما أن (أحدثه الباري جل وعلا، ومحال أحداثه قبل إحداث علمه وقدرته لما أن) إيجاده بدون القدرة عليه والعلم به محال، وإذا كان القول بإحداثه علمه وقدرته ينقسم إلى هذه الأقسام وهي كلها داخلة في حيز المحال كان محالا في نفسه. ونشرح هذا الكلام بأتم من هذا إذا انتهينا إلى إبطال قول الكرامية – إن الله تعالى محل للحوادث - وإبطال وقول القدرية - إن كلام الله تعالى محدث إن شاء الله تعالى –
The locus of accidents is a proof of its createdness in itself, and by the acceptance of prime matter for accidents we have argued for their being created. As for if He created them not in a locus, that is impossible, due to the impossibility of attributes subsisting by themselves. And if this were permissible for knowledge and power, it would be permissible for motion and rest and blackness and whiteness. And because if they subsisted by themselves, they would not be, by being power and knowledge for Him, more appropriate than being power and knowledge for another. And as for if He created them in another locus, that is impossible, because it necessitates that the locus in which they subsist is the knowing and powerful one, not Allah the Exalted, just as when He creates motion, rest, blackness, and whiteness in a locus, the locus becomes the moving, resting, black, white thing, not Allah who created them; so likewise this. And because either He created them in another locus that is eternal, and the assertion of an eternal subsisting in essence besides Allah is impossible as has passed. Or He created them in a locus that is created? [...] And either He brought them into existence, and it is impossible to bring them into existence before creating His knowledge and power because bringing into existence without ability and knowledge is impossible. And when the assertion of His creating His knowledge and power divides into these divisions, all of which fall within the realm of impossibility, it is impossible in itself. And we will explain this statement more fully than this when we reach the refutation of the Karramiyya's statement that Allah is a locus for accidents, and the refutation of the Qadariyya's statement that the speech of Allah is created, if Allah wills.
Source pages p. 364

Commentary
This passage is a proof that God's attributes (knowledge and power) cannot be created. The author examines three possibilities for how God could create His own knowledge and power: (1) in the same locus (the thing qualified), (2) not in a locus, or (3) in another locus. Each is refuted. For (1), the author says that if attributes were created in the same locus, that locus would need to be a body, but bodies are created, leading to circularity. For (2), attributes cannot subsist by themselves; that would imply they are independent substances, which is impossible for accidents. For (3), if created in another locus, that locus would become the knowing and powerful entity, not God. Also, if that locus is eternal, it would be a second eternal, which is impossible. Thus all possibilities are impossible, so the original claim (that God creates His own knowledge and power) is impossible. The author then notes that this will be expanded when refuting the Karramiyya and Qadariyya.

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: That God's attributes could be created in a different substrate (like the Preserved Tablet) without transferring divinity.
Correction: The argument shows that any substrate in which attributes subsist becomes the qualified entity. So if God's knowledge and power were created in another locus, that locus would become the knowing and powerful one, not God.

D) Because God cannot create in a locus.

Key Takeaway
God's attributes of knowledge and power cannot be created in any way because every possible scenario leads to a logical contradiction.

Will you confess that and surrender those areas to Him before the day ends?

Attributes Are Not Other Than God and Knowledge of the Non-Existent
Refutation of the doubt that attributes are other than God; discussion of pre-eternal knowledge.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand that the divine attributes are not separate entities from God, and that the majority of Muslims affirm God's eternal knowledge includes knowledge of non-existent things, contrary to some early theologians.

Core Idea
Attributes are not separate from God; He knows all things eternally, even non-existents.

In this passage, the author tackles a subtle doubt about the eternity of attributes. He clarifies that attributes are not 'others' (aghyar) of God, thus avoiding any implication of multiple eternal entities. He then presents a historical disagreement about the scope of God's pre-eternal knowledge: does it include non-existent future things? The mainstream position affirms yes, while some early theologians like Hisham ibn al-Hakam and Hisham ibn Amr denied it.

Guided Path
1
Read the full passage carefully
Read the Arabic passage and its translation. Notice that it begins with a heading-like statement and then two main sections: a refutation and a report of disagreement.
The passage ends mid-sentence, but the main points are clear.
2
Identify the refutation of the doubt
Find the sentence that states the doubt (shubha) and the refutation. Understand why the doubt is invalid: because attributes are not 'other than' God.
The term 'aghyar' (others) is key—it implies separate entities.
3
Examine the disagreement about knowledge
Read the second part where people differ on whether God knew things other than His essence in pre-eternity. Note the mainstream view and the opposing view of the two Hishams.
The mainstream allows knowledge of the non-existent (ma'dum).

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
[الصفات ليست بأغيار الله تعالى وهو يعلم ذاته وصفاته وما وراء ذلك ]: وشبهته أن القول بقدم غير الله تعالى محال باطلة، لما أن الصفات ليست بأغيار الله تعالى على ما نبين بعد هذا - إن شاء الله تعالى. فإذا ثبت أنه تعالى كان في الأزل عالما اختلف الناس أنه هل كان عالما بما وراء ذاته. قال كل من أثبت الصانع إنه كان عالما بذاته وصفاته، وبما وراء ذلك مما يكون وإن كان العالم معدوما بعد، وجوزوا دخول المعدوم تحت العلم. وقال هشام بن الحكم أحد رؤساء الروافض وهشام بن عمرو أحد رؤساء المعتزلة: إنه لم يكن عالما بما وراء ذاته إذ كل ذلك كان معدوما، وتعلق العلم بالمعدوم
[Attributes are not others of Allah the Exalted, and He knows His essence, attributes, and what is beyond that]: His doubt that the assertion of an eternal other than Allah is impossible is invalid, because the attributes are not others (aghyar) of Allah, as we will clarify after this, if Allah wills. So when it is established that the Exalted was in pre-eternity knowing, people differed as to whether He was knowing of what is beyond His essence. Everyone who affirmed the Creator said that He was knowing of His essence and attributes, and of what is beyond that which will come to be even if the world is still non-existent, and they allowed non-existent things to fall under knowledge. And Hisham ibn al-Hakam, one of the heads of the Rawafid, and Hisham ibn Amr, one of the heads of the Mu'tazila, said: He was not knowing of what is beyond His essence, since all that was non-existent, and knowledge's relation to the non-existent
Source pages p. 365

Commentary
This passage first refutes a doubt (shubha) that the assertion of an eternal other than God is impossible. The author says the doubt is invalid because the attributes are not 'others' (aghyar) of God—they are not separate entities. Then the author moves to a related discussion: since it is established that God is eternally knowing, there is disagreement about whether He knew things other than Himself in pre-eternity. The majority (all who affirm the Creator) hold that God knew His essence, attributes, and all future things even when they were non-existent, and they allow knowledge to relate to non-existents. In contrast, Hisham ibn al-Hakam (a Rafidi leader) and Hisham ibn Amr (a Mu'tazili leader) denied that God knew anything other than Himself in pre-eternity because those things were non-existent, and they denied that knowledge can relate to non-existents. The passage ends mid-sentence, likely continuing on the next page.

God's Attributes Are Not Other Than Him
Nasafi dismisses the objection that eternal attributes imply other eternal beings.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand why Nasafi refutes the claim that God's attributes are 'other than Him' and how this preserves tawhid.

Core Idea
Attributes are not separate entities; they are not 'other than God'.

This lesson tackles a critical objection in Islamic theology: if God's attributes are eternal, doesn't that mean there are multiple eternal beings? Nasafi quickly dismisses this, stating that attributes are not 'other than' God. Let's examine this brief but profound refutation.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage
Read the Arabic passage along with its translation. Notice that the heading already states the conclusion: attributes are not other than God.
2
Identify the objection
The objection is that saying attributes are pre-eternal (qadim) would imply something other than God is eternal. Why would someone think that?
The objector assumes attributes are 'other than' God.
3
Understand the refutation
Nasafi refutes by asserting that attributes are not 'other than' God (aghyar). They are not separate entities. He promises a fuller explanation later.
4
Reflect on the implication
If attributes are not other than God, then affirming their eternity does not introduce multiplicity. This preserves the oneness of God.

[الصفات ليست بأغيار الله تعالى وهو يعلم ذاته وصفاته وما وراء ذلك ]: وشبهته أن القول بقدم غير الله تعالى محال باطلة، لما أن الصفات ليست بأغيار الله تعالى على ما نبين بعد هذا - إن شاء الله تعالى.
[Attributes are not other than God Almighty, and He knows His essence, His attributes, and what is beyond that]: And his doubt that the statement of the pre-eternity of other than God Almighty is impossible is false, because attributes are not other than God Almighty, as we will explain after this - if God Almighty wills.
Source pages p. 365

Commentary
This passage is a brief refutation of an objection. The heading states the position: God's attributes are not other than Him (i.e., they are not distinct entities that could be said to be 'other than God'). The objection being refuted is the claim that saying attributes are pre-eternal would mean something other than God is pre-eternal, which is impossible. The author dismisses this by asserting that attributes are not 'other' (aghyar) than God—they are not separate existences. The full explanation is promised for later.

?
You will one day stand before God and be judged by His justice. But if justice is not other than Him, does that make the prospect more terrifying or more hopeful? How does this truth affect your repentance tonight?

The debate on God's knowledge of the non-existent
Nasafi records differing views on God's knowledge of the non-existent.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the main positions in the debate about whether God knows non-existent things before they exist, and how scriptural verses were used to argue against pre-creative knowledge.

Core Idea
God's knowledge of the non-existent was a disputed issue with major theological stakes.

This passage from Nasafi's Tabṣirat al-Adilla presents a key theological debate: does God know things before they exist? The majority of theologians affirmed that God knows all things, even non-existent future entities, while some prominent figures denied this, arguing that knowledge can only attach to existent things. Nasafi records their views and the scriptural proofs they advanced.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage and translation
Read the Arabic passage once without trying to analyse it. Then read the translation. Let the author's own rhythm come through before you interpret.
Notice that the passage begins with a premise and then presents differing views.
2
Identify the two main positions
Find the majority view (all who affirm the Maker) and the opposing view of Hisham ibn al-Hakam, Hisham ibn Amr, and Jahm. Note how each position is defended.
3
Note the scriptural evidence
The opponents cite several Quranic verses. List the verses mentioned and understand how they argue from them that God does not know the non-existent.
These verses include tests and expressions of 'knowing' that seem to imply acquisition.
4
Reflect on theological stakes
Ask yourself why this debate matters. How does it relate to the attribute of omniscience and the interpretation of Quranic language?
The author does not refute these arguments here, but the debate is important for understanding divine attributes.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
فإذا ثبت أنه تعالى كان في الأزل عالما اختلف الناس أنه هل كان عالما بما وراء ذاته. قال كل من أثبت الصانع إنه كان عالما بذاته وصفاته، وبما وراء ذلك مما يكون وإن كان العالم معدوما بعد، وجوزوا دخول المعدوم تحت العلم. وقال هشام بن الحكم أحد رؤساء الروافض وهشام بن عمرو أحد رؤساء المعتزلة: إنه لم يكن عالما بما وراء ذاته إذ كل ذلك كان معدوما، وتعلق العلم بالمعدوم محال وروى أبو الحسين (الخياط) عن جهم أيضا أنه كان يقول : إن الله تعالى يعلم الشيء في حالة حدوثه، وأحال العلم بالمعدوم. لكن ما روينا من الرواية عنه أثبت فإن مشايخنا كذا رووا عنه - وذكر عبد القاهر البغدادي أن جماعة من المتكلمين حكوا عنه أنه قال : إن الله تعالى يعلم الأشياء قبل حدوثها بعلم أحدثه قبلها. وهذا نص أنه كان يجوز كون المعدوم معلوما. وتعلق من زعم أن الله تعالى لا يعلم المعدوم، وإنما يعلم ما حدث عنه حدوثه قوله : يبلُوَكُمْ أَيُّكُمْ أَحْسَنُ عَمَلاً والابتلاء إنما يكون ليظهر ما لم يكن ظاهرا، وتحصيل علم لم يكن حاصلا بحال من ابتلاه به ـــ ولقوله تعالى: وَمَا جَعَلْنَا الْقِبْلَةَ الَّتِي كُنتَ عَلَيْهَا إِلَّا لِنَعْلَمَ مَن يَتَّبِعُ الرَّسُولَ مِمَّن يَنقَلِبُ عَلَى عَقِبَيْهِ ولقوله تعالى: لَعَلَّهُ يَتَذَكَّرُ أَوْ يَخشَف ()() لعله يزد (1) لَعَلَّهُ يَزكَ واستعمال لفظة الترجي ممن كان عالما بالأمر محال . وقد قال تعالى لِنَنظُرَ كَيْفَ تَعْمَلُونَ ، وقال تعالى : لِنَعْلَمَ أَيُّ الْحِزْبَيْنِ أَحْصَى لِمَا لَبِثُوا أَمَدًا وغير ذلك من الآيات وهي تدل كلها على أنه لا يكون عالما بالمعدوم ما لم يوجد.
When it is established that He was knowing in pre-eternity, people differed: was He knowing of what is beyond His essence? Everyone who affirmed the Maker said that He was knowing of His essence, His attributes, and what is beyond that of things that will be, even though the world was still non-existent, and they permitted the non-existent to fall under knowledge. Hisham ibn al-Hakam, one of the leaders of the Rafidah, and Hisham ibn Amr, one of the leaders of the Mu'tazilah, said: He was not knowing of what is beyond His essence, because all that was non-existent, and the connection of knowledge to the non-existent is impossible. And Abu al-Husayn al-Khayyat narrated from Jahm that he used to say: God knows the thing at the time of its occurrence, and he deemed knowledge of the non-existent impossible. But what we have narrated from him is more firmly established, for our masters thus narrated from him. And Abd al-Qahir al-Baghdadi mentioned that a group of theologians reported from him that he said: God knows things before their occurrence with a knowledge He creates before them. This is a text that he permitted the non-existent to be known. And those who claim that God does not know the non-existent but only knows what occurs at its occurrence adduce His saying: 'That He may test you which of you is best in deed' – and testing is only to make apparent what was not apparent, and to acquire knowledge that was not present on the part of the one tested by it – and His saying: 'And We did not make the qiblah which you used to face except that We might know who follows the Messenger from who turns back on his heels' – and His saying: 'Perhaps he will remember or fear' – and the use of the word of expectation from one who knows the matter is impossible. And He said: 'That We may see how you act' – and He said: 'That We might know which of the two parties is more accurate in counting what they have tarried' – and other verses, all of which indicate that He is not knowing of the non-existent until it exists.
Source pages p. 365

Commentary
This passage presents the theological debate about whether God knows things before they exist (i.e., knowledge of the non-existent, al-ma'dum). After establishing that God is knowing in pre-eternity, the author notes that people differed on whether that knowledge extends beyond His essence. The majority (all who affirm the Maker) held that God knows His essence, attributes, and all future things even while they are non-existent; they allowed that the non-existent can be an object of knowledge. Two figures—Hisham ibn al-Hakam (a leader of the Rafidah/Shi'a) and Hisham ibn Amr (a leader of the Mu'tazila)—denied this, arguing that knowledge of the non-existent is impossible because the non-existent has no reality. Jahm is also reported to have denied knowledge of the non-existent, but the author notes a more reliable report that Jahm allowed a created knowledge before events. The author then presents the arguments of those who deny pre-creative knowledge: they cite verses of the Quran that speak of God testing or wanting to know something, which they interpret as implying that God acquires knowledge at the time of events. The author lists several verses (based on the English translation, the Arabic has them) and concludes that these verses seem to support the view that God does not know the non-existent until it exists. However, the author does not endorse this view here; it is followed by a refutation.

Key Terms
المعدوم
العلم
القديم
هشام بن الحكم
هشام بن عمرو
جهم

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Denying God's knowledge of the non-existent is a trivial theological point.
Correction: This debate was central to discussions of divine attributes and the interpretation of Quranic verses about divine knowledge, with significant implications for the nature of omniscience.

Checkpoint

Key Takeaway
The majority of theologians affirmed that God knows all things, including non-existent future entities, while a minority denied this based on the impossibility of knowing non-existents.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?

Why Perfect Action Requires Prior Knowledge
Nasafi refutes the denial of God's knowledge of the non-existent.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand why kalam theologians argue that God must know things before they exist, based on the principle that perfect craftsmanship demands prior knowledge.

Core Idea
Perfect action proves perfect knowledge—and that knowledge must be before the act.

This lesson engages with a foundational argument in Islamic theology: the claim that God cannot know non-existent things contradicts both reason and religion. Nasafi presents the consensus of theologians that a perfectly crafted action necessarily implies that its doer had knowledge of it beforehand. This argument is essential for understanding divine omniscience and the rationality of creation.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage and translation
Read the Arabic source once and then the literal translation. Notice how Nasafi frames the argument as a consensus of the majority of theologians.
The passage is cut off at the end, but the main idea is clear.
2
Identify the key claim and the supporting analogy
The claim: denying knowledge of the non-existent is irrational. The support: a precise and perfect action indicates knowledge of the doer, and that knowledge must exist before the action.
Think of a craftsman who produces a fine object—he must have planned it beforehand.
3
Reflect on the logical necessity
Why is prior knowledge necessary? Without it, the action cannot be precise and perfect. Sound intellects accept this. This shows that God's knowledge of non-existent things is rationally required.
This argument refutes those who limit God's knowledge to what exists.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وعامة المتكلمين قالوا: إن القول بخروج المعدوم من أن يكون معلوما يناقض العقل، ويرد على قواعد الدين بالإبطال وبيان ذلك : أن كون الفعل محكما متقنا يدل على علم فاعله به على ما بينا. وتقررت صحة ذلك في العقول السليمة حتى إن من توقع ممن لا علم له تحصيل صورة مؤنقة أو صفة بديعة عجيبة، عد متجاهلا وشرط ذلك هو العلم به قبل وجوده لا بعد وجوده ليحصله على حسب ما علمه من
And the generality of theologians said: The statement that the non-existent is excluded from being known contradicts reason and leads to the invalidation of the foundations of religion. The explanation of that is: that an action being precise and perfect indicates the knowledge of its doer, as we have explained. And the correctness of that is established in sound intellects, to the extent that if one expects from someone who has no knowledge the production of an elegant form or a wonderful, amazing quality, he is considered ignorant. And the condition for that is knowledge of it before its existence, not after its existence, so that he may produce it according to what he knew of
Source pages p. 366

Commentary
This passage begins the refutation of those who deny God's knowledge of the non-existent. The author summarizes the position of the majority of theologians: the claim that the non-existent cannot be known is irrational and undermines the foundations of religion. The key argument is that a precise and perfect action ('محكم متقن') necessarily indicates that its doer has knowledge of it before executing it—this principle is based on earlier proofs. The author adds that sound intellects accept this: if someone were to produce a beautiful form or an amazing quality, and we know he had no prior knowledge of it, we would consider him ignorant or pretending. The condition for production is prior knowledge, not post-existence knowledge. The passage ends abruptly, but it clearly presents the core of the argument: perfect craftsmanship presupposes pre-existent knowledge.

Key Terms

المعدوم (al-maʿdūm)
الفعل المحكم المتقن (al-fiʿl al-muḥkam al-mutqan)
العلم (al-ʿilm)

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some think that God's knowledge is like human knowledge—acquired after the fact.
Correction: This argument shows that perfect action requires prior knowledge, which is a rational necessity; therefore, God must know things before they exist.

Checkpoint

God's perfect creation demands that He knows everything before He creates it, a principle established by reason and consensus of theologians.

Perfect Actions Prove Prior Knowledge
Argument that perfect actions indicate the doer's prior knowledge.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand why perfect actions necessarily imply the doer's prior knowledge, and why that knowledge must exist before the action.

Core Idea
A perfect action requires prior knowledge; knowledge after the fact is useless.

The majority of theologians present a powerful argument from common sense: when we see a well-crafted object, we instinctively know its maker had prior knowledge. This lesson examines that argument and shows why denying God's knowledge of non-existents collapses under this reasoning.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage on perfect actions
Read the Arabic passage carefully (up to 'وهذا محال'). Note how the argument builds from the observed perfection of actions to the necessity of prior knowledge.
The passage uses the example of expecting an elegant image from someone with no knowledge.
2
Understand the condition of knowledge
The passage stresses that knowledge must be before the existence of the act, not after. Ask yourself why knowledge after the act would be ineffective.
Knowledge after doesn't contribute to the act's perfection.
3
Identify the conclusion
The conclusion is that denying knowledge of the non-existent (before existence) leads to the absurd claim that perfect actions occur without knowledge.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وعامة المتكلمين قالوا: إن القول بخروج المعدوم من أن يكون معلوما يناقض العقل، ويرد على قواعد الدين بالإبطال. وبيان ذلك: أن كون الفعل محكما متقنا يدل على علم فاعله به على ما بينا. وتقررت صحة ذلك في العقول السليمة حتى إن من توقع ممن لا علم له تحصيل صورة مؤنقة أو صفة بديعة عجيبة، عد متجاهلا وشرط ذلك هو العلم به قبل وجوده لا بعد وجوده ليحصله على حسب ما علمه من الإتقان والجودة لا على ما يضاده من الوهي والرداءة. فأما بعدما حصل ووجد لا عن علم، فإنه لا يصير بحصول العلم مقتنا محكما ووجود العلم به بعد وجوده مما لا أثر له في إثبات صفة الإحكام والإتقان فيه. فمن لم يجوز العلم بالمعدوم، جعل وجود الأفعال المحكمة والصنائع البديعة لا عن علم لفاعله به وهذا محال. ولأن كل قاصد تحصيل شيء يكون ذلك الشيء ثابتا في علمه يحصله على حسب به، لولا ذلك لما أمكنه تحصيله. عرف صحة هذا كل من يرجع إلى نفسه معرفة لا يسوغه عقله جحودها وإنكارها. وكذا كل من يفعل فعلا لعاقبة يعد حكيما، ومن يفعل لا لعاقبة حميدة يعد سفيها. ولو لم يكن العلم بالعواقب ثابتا لما اتصف فعل ما بحكمة ولا سفه ولا فاعل ما بحكيم. وفي شيوع هذا الوصف للأفعال والفاعلين يوجب بطلان قول هذا القائل.
And the majority of the theologians said: The statement that the non-existent is excluded from being known contradicts reason and rebuts the foundations of religion by invalidation. And the explanation of that: The fact that an action is firmly made and perfect indicates the knowledge of its doer of it, as we have explained. And the correctness of that is established in sound intellects to the point that whoever expects from one who has no knowledge the production of an elegant image or a wonderful, amazing quality is considered feigning ignorance, and the condition of that is knowledge of it before its existence, not after its existence, so that he produces it according to what he knew of perfection and quality, not according to what is opposite to it of weakness and poorness. As for after it has been obtained and existed without knowledge, then it does not become, through the acquisition of knowledge, perfectly made and sound; and the existence of knowledge of it after its existence has no effect in establishing the attribute of firmness and perfection in it. So whoever does not allow knowledge of the non-existent, makes the existence of firm actions and wonderful crafts occur without knowledge by their doer, and this is impossible. And because every one who intends to obtain something, that thing is established in his knowledge and he obtains it accordingly; were it not for that, he would not be able to obtain it. Everyone who consults himself knows the correctness of this, his intellect does not allow its denial and rejection. And likewise, everyone who does an act for a consequence is considered wise, and whoever does not do it for a praiseworthy consequence is considered foolish. And if knowledge of consequences were not established, no act would be described as wisdom or foolishness, nor any doer as wise. And the prevalence of this description for actions and doers necessitates the invalidity of this statement.
Source pages p. 366

Commentary
This passage is the refutation by the majority of theologians. They assert that denying knowledge of the non-existent contradicts both reason and religion. The argument proceeds in stages: 1) The perfect construction of any action proves that its doer must have had prior knowledge. This is intuitively recognized: if someone produces a well-crafted object without prior knowledge, they would be considered feigning ignorance. 2) Knowledge must exist before the act, not after, because knowledge after the act does not contribute to the act's perfection. 3) Therefore, to deny that God knows non-existent things is to claim that God's actions are not based on knowledge, which is absurd. 4) A further argument: every agent who acts for a purpose must know that purpose beforehand, otherwise the action cannot be described as wise or foolish. Since actions are clearly attributed to wisdom, the agent must have prior knowledge. 5) The widespread ascription of wisdom to actions and agents refutes the denial of knowledge of non-existents.

Key Terms
العلم بالمعدوم
الفعل المحكم
الإتقان

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: That knowledge can only be of existent things.
Correction: The passage argues that perfect actions require knowledge before existence, so the non-existent must be known.

Checkpoint
According to the majority argument, what would someone be considered if they expect a beautifully crafted object from a person with no knowledge?
A) Wise.
B) Foolish.
C) Feigning ignorance.
D) A philosopher.

Key Takeaway
Perfect actions can only come from prior knowledge; therefore, knowledge of non-existents is necessary.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you observe the intricate design of the universe, do you truly pause to recognize that it could only come from God's eternal knowledge of it before it existed, or do you merely pass by without reflection? Commit today to contemplate one sign of His perfection as a proof of His knowledge.
?
This argument demonstrates that denying God's knowledge of the non-existent leads to absurdity. Does your heart fully submit to the fact that Allah knows everything before it happens, including your own actions? How should this awareness change your intentions and deeds right now?
?
The passage equates expecting perfect work without knowledge to feigning ignorance. Are there areas in your life where you act as if God does not foresee your choices, or where you doubt His prior knowledge? Repent and reaffirm your belief in His all-encompassing knowledge.

Purposeful Action Proves Knowledge of Consequences
Argument that purposeful action proves knowledge of consequences.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how the attribution of wisdom or foolishness to actions implies the agent's prior knowledge of consequences.

Core Idea
Wisdom and foolishness depend on knowledge of consequences.

The majority's argument continues by considering purposeful action. If someone acts for a consequence, they are called wise; if not, foolish. But this distinction only makes sense if the agent knows the consequences beforehand. Thus, denying knowledge of future (non-existent) consequences undermines the very basis of describing actions as wise or foolish.

Guided Path
1
Read the second part of the passage
Read from 'ولأن كل قاصد' to the end. Focus on the connection between acting for a consequence and knowledge.
2
Analyze the wisdom/foolishness distinction
Note that an act is considered wise if done for a good consequence, foolish if not. This implies the agent knew the consequence.
The passage says 'كل من يفعل فعلا لعاقبة يعد حكيما'.
3
Apply the argument to God
Since God's actions are universally described as wise (full of wisdom), He must know the consequences, which are non-existent at the time of creation.
This refutes the denial of knowledge of non-existents.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وعامة المتكلمين قالوا: إن القول بخروج المعدوم من أن يكون معلوما يناقض العقل، ويرد على قواعد الدين بالإبطال. وبيان ذلك: أن كون الفعل محكما متقنا يدل على علم فاعله به على ما بينا. وتقررت صحة ذلك في العقول السليمة حتى إن من توقع ممن لا علم له تحصيل صورة مؤنقة أو صفة بديعة عجيبة، عد متجاهلا وشرط ذلك هو العلم به قبل وجوده لا بعد وجوده ليحصله على حسب ما علمه من الإتقان والجودة لا على ما يضاده من الوهي والرداءة. فأما بعدما حصل ووجد لا عن علم، فإنه لا يصير بحصول العلم مقتنا محكما ووجود العلم به بعد وجوده مما لا أثر له في إثبات صفة الإحكام والإتقان فيه. فمن لم يجوز العلم بالمعدوم، جعل وجود الأفعال المحكمة والصنائع البديعة لا عن علم لفاعله به وهذا محال. ولأن كل قاصد تحصيل شيء يكون ذلك الشيء ثابتا في علمه يحصله على حسب به، لولا ذلك لما أمكنه تحصيله. عرف صحة هذا كل من يرجع إلى نفسه معرفة لا يسوغه عقله جحودها وإنكارها. وكذا كل من يفعل فعلا لعاقبة يعد حكيما، ومن يفعل لا لعاقبة حميدة يعد سفيها. ولو لم يكن العلم بالعواقب ثابتا لما اتصف فعل ما بحكمة ولا سفه ولا فاعل ما بحكيم. وفي شيوع هذا الوصف للأفعال والفاعلين يوجب بطلان قول هذا القائل.
And the majority of the theologians said: The statement that the non-existent is excluded from being known contradicts reason and rebuts the foundations of religion by invalidation. And the explanation of that: The fact that an action is firmly made and perfect indicates the knowledge of its doer of it, as we have explained. And the correctness of that is established in sound intellects to the point that whoever expects from one who has no knowledge the production of an elegant image or a wonderful, amazing quality is considered feigning ignorance, and the condition of that is knowledge of it before its existence, not after its existence, so that he produces it according to what he knew of perfection and quality, not according to what is opposite to it of weakness and poorness. As for after it has been obtained and existed without knowledge, then it does not become, through the acquisition of knowledge, perfectly made and sound; and the existence of knowledge of it after its existence has no effect in establishing the attribute of firmness and perfection in it. So whoever does not allow knowledge of the non-existent, makes the existence of firm actions and wonderful crafts occur without knowledge by their doer, and this is impossible. And because every one who intends to obtain something, that thing is established in his knowledge and he obtains it accordingly; were it not for that, he would not be able to obtain it. Everyone who consults himself knows the correctness of this, his intellect does not allow its denial and rejection. And likewise, everyone who does an act for a consequence is considered wise, and whoever does not do it for a praiseworthy consequence is considered foolish. And if knowledge of consequences were not established, no act would be described as wisdom or foolishness, nor any doer as wise. And the prevalence of this description for actions and doers necessitates the invalidity of this statement.
Source pages p. 366

Commentary
This passage is the refutation by the majority of theologians. They assert that denying knowledge of the non-existent contradicts both reason and religion. The argument proceeds in stages: 1) The perfect construction of any action proves that its doer must have had prior knowledge. This is intuitively recognized: if someone produces a well-crafted object without prior knowledge, they would be considered feigning ignorance. 2) Knowledge must exist before the act, not after, because knowledge after the act does not contribute to the act's perfection. 3) Therefore, to deny that God knows non-existent things is to claim that God's actions are not based on knowledge, which is absurd. 4) A further argument: every agent who acts for a purpose must know that purpose beforehand, otherwise the action cannot be described as wise or foolish. Since actions are clearly attributed to wisdom, the agent must have prior knowledge. 5) The widespread ascription of wisdom to actions and agents refutes the denial of knowledge of non-existents.

Key Terms
الحكمة
السفه
العلم بالعواقب

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: That actions can be described as wise or foolish without implying prior knowledge of outcomes.
Correction: The passage shows that wisdom/foolishness are only meaningful if the agent knows the consequences beforehand.

Checkpoint
According to the passage, what is required for an action to be described as wise?
A) The action must be perfect.
B) The agent must have knowledge of the consequences beforehand.
C) The action must be done without any purpose.
D) The agent must be human.

Key Takeaway
The widespread description of actions as wise proves that God knows non-existent consequences.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you act each day, do you deliberately consider the ultimate consequences in the sight of Allah? If not, what stops you from doing so? Commit today to pause before any major decision and ask: 'What outcome in the afterlife am I aiming for?'
?
The description 'wise' is only valid if you know the consequences. How many of your recent actions would be called foolish if you lacked knowledge of their outcomes? Repent for carelessness and resolve to seek knowledge before acting.
?
If God's wisdom required knowledge of non-existent consequences, how does that deepen your trust in His plan even when you see no wisdom in your trials? Write down one trial you face and affirm that Allah knows its consequence, so you can submit to His wisdom.

The Necessity of God's Knowledge for Perfect Creation
Argument that perfect actions require prior knowledge and al-Maturidi's proof from creation

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand why perfect creation necessarily requires prior knowledge and how al-Maturidi proves that God has knowledge of all things before their existence.

Core Idea
Perfect creation demands perfect prior knowledge.

This passage tackles a fundamental question: does God need to know things before they exist? The author argues that denying such knowledge leads to absurdity, and then presents al-Maturidi's proof from the order and purpose evident in creation. You will see how reason itself confirms that perfect actions cannot come from ignorance.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage and translation
Read the Arabic passage once without overanalyzing. Then read the literal translation to grasp the overall argument.
Notice the shift from general rational argument to al-Maturidi's specific proof.
2
Identify the two main parts
The passage has two sections: a general rational argument (first half) and al-Maturidi's proof from creation (second half). Label them mentally.
3
Understand the critique of denying knowledge of the non-existent
The author argues that if an action comes into existence without prior knowledge, later knowledge cannot make it perfect. Therefore, denying that God knows things before they exist forces one to claim that perfect actions arise from ignorance—which is impossible.
This is the core logical move.
4
Grasp al-Maturidi's proof from creation
Al-Maturidi points to created substances that are not directly tested in the trials of the tested ones, and to things created for permanence along with their means of sustenance. This intricate order shows that the Creator knew the nature and needs of everything.
Connect this back to the need for prior knowledge.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
فأما بعدما حصل ووجد لا عن علم، فإنه لا يصير بحصول العلم مقتنا محكما ووجود العلم به بعد وجوده مما لا أثر له في إثبات صفة الإحكام والإتقان فيه، فمن لم يجوز العلم بالمعدوم، جعل وجود الأفعال المحكمة والصنائع البديعة لا عن علم لفاعله به وهذا محال. ولأن كل قاصد تحصيل شيء يكون ذلك الشيء ثابتا في علمه يحصله على حسب به، لولا ذلك لما أمكنه تحصيله عرف صحة هذا كل من يرجع إلى نفسه معرفة لا يسوغه عقله جحودها وإنكارها. وكذا كل من يفعل فعلا لعاقبة يعد حكيما، ومن يفعل لا لعاقبة حميدة يعد سفيها، ولو لم يكن العلم بالعواقب ثابتا لما اتصف فعل ما بحكمة ولا سفه ولا فاعل ما بحكيم، وفي شيوع هذا الوصف للأفعال والفاعلين يوجب بطلان قول هذا القائل. مما لرأي الماتريدي: واحتج الشيخ أبو منصور رحمه الله تعالى فقال : إنه تعالى إذ خلق كل الجواهر التي لا تمتحن في مصالح الممتحنين، وخلق كل شيء أريد به البقاء مع خلق ما به بقاؤه علم أنه كان ممن يعلم كيفية كل شيء وحاجته، وما به القوام والمعاش ولا قوة إلا بالله.
As for after (an action) has occurred and come into existence without knowledge, then it does not become, by the acquisition of knowledge, a precisely made and perfect (thing); and the existence of knowledge of it after its existence has no effect in establishing the attribute of soundness and perfection in it. So whoever does not permit knowledge of the non-existent has made the existence of perfect actions and marvelous crafts without knowledge by their doer, and this is impossible. And because every seeker of attaining something has that thing established in his knowledge and produces it accordingly; were it not for that, he would not be able to produce it. Anyone who consults his own self knows the correctness of this — a knowledge that his intellect does not permit him to deny or reject. Likewise, everyone who does an act for a consequence is considered wise, and whoever does not do it for a praiseworthy consequence is considered foolish. And if knowledge of consequences were not established, no act would be described as wise or foolish, nor any doer as wise. And the prevalence of this description for acts and doers necessitates the invalidity of this speaker's statement. From the view of al-Maturidi: And Shaykh Abu Mansur — may Allah have mercy on him — argued, saying: Indeed, when He created all the substances that are not tested in the benefits of those who are tested, and created everything intended for permanence along with creating that by which it is sustained, it is known that He was one who knows the how of everything and its need, and that by which stability and livelihood are achieved. And there is no power except by Allah.
Source pages p. 367

Commentary
This passage is a proof that God's knowledge is necessary for the perfection of creation. It begins by stating that if an action exists without prior knowledge, subsequent knowledge cannot make it perfect. The author then argues that anyone who denies knowledge of the non-existent (i.e., that God knows things before they exist) is forced to claim that perfect actions arise from ignorance, which is impossible. Next, the author appeals to common sense: anyone who intends to produce something has it in his knowledge first; otherwise, he could not produce it. Similarly, acts done with a goal in mind are called wise, and acts without a good goal are called foolish; this distinction presupposes knowledge of consequences. If knowledge of consequences were not possible, these descriptions would be meaningless. The prevalence of these descriptions in everyday language refutes the opponent's position. Then the author presents al-Maturidi's specific proof: God created substances that are not tested in the trials of the tested ones, and He created everything intended to persist along with its means of sustenance — this demonstrates that He knows the nature and needs of everything, and that He is the sustainer.

Key Terms
العلم بالمعدوم
الإحكام والإتقان
الحكيم
الجواهر
الممتحنين

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: God only knows things after they come into existence.
Correction: The passage argues that perfect creation requires prior knowledge; otherwise perfect actions would arise from ignorance, which is impossible.

Checkpoint

A) Because perfect actions cannot arise from ignorance.
B) Because God cannot know future events.
C) Because the intellect cannot accept such knowledge.
D) Because al-Maturidi said so.

Key Takeaway
Without prior knowledge, perfect creation is impossible; al-Maturidi's proof from the order of creation confirms that God knows all things before they exist.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
You have just read that God's perfect creation requires His prior knowledge of every detail. Your own existence—your body, your circumstances—is part of that perfect creation. Do you truly believe that God knew every moment of your life before you were born? How would that belief change the way you face a trial you are avoiding today? Commit to one specific action this week that reflects trust in His knowledge.
?
The passage says that actions done without knowledge cannot be made perfect later. Think of an area in your life where you act impulsively, expecting to 'fix it later' with knowledge. What is that area, and what would it look like to seek God's guidance (knowledge) before you act? Write down one step you will take today to prioritize knowing His will before you move.
?
Al-Maturidi points out that God created countless things that are never tested, solely for the benefit of those who are tested. Look around you—your home, your health, the air you breathe. How many of these blessings are you taking for granted? What is one blessing you have not thanked God for today? Before you sleep tonight, repent for your ingratitude and thank Him specifically for that blessing, knowing that He created it for you out of His perfect knowledge.
