The Impossibility of Denying God's Foreknowledge
Opening dilemma and denial branch.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand that denying God's foreknowledge contradicts explicit Quranic predictions and constitutes clear disbelief.

Core Idea
Denying God's foreknowledge means rejecting hundreds of fulfilled prophecies.

The author begins by posing a simple question: Did God inform about future events? If someone denies this, they must reject all the predictions in the Quran and earlier scriptures. The passage then lists several examples of fulfilled prophecies, showing that such denial is impossible for a believer.

Guided Path
1
Read the opening dilemma
Read the first sentence carefully: the question 'Did God inform about future events?' sets up the whole argument.
2
Identify the denial branch
Notice that if the opponent says 'No', they must reject all the prophecies listed.
The list includes prophecies about Prophet Muhammad, the conquest of Mecca, etc.
3
Understand the conclusion
The passage declares that denial of these explicit verses is clear disbelief.
This is the first horn of the dilemma.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ويقال لهؤلاء: إن الله تعالى هل أخبر عما يكون في المستقبل؟ فإن قالوا: لا. فقد أنكروا ما أخبر الله تعالى الأنبياء المتقدمين عليهم السلام من أنباء نبينا محمد عليه السلام، وبشارة عيسى عليه السلام به على ما نطق به الكتاب بقوله تعالى: ﴿ وَمُبَشِّرًا بِرَسُولِ يَأْتِي مِنْ بَعْدِى اسْمُهُ أَحَمَدُ ﴾ وما أنبأ الله تعالى في القرآن عن الكائنات من نحو قوله تعالى: ﴿ سَتُدْعَوْنَ إِلَى قَوْمٍ أُولِي بَأْسٍ شَدِيدٍ ﴾ وقوله تعالى: لَتَدْخُلُنَّ الْمَسْجِدَ الْحَرَامَ إِن شَاءَ اللهُ آمِنِينَ ﴿ وقوله تعالى: وَعَدَ اللهُ الَّذِينَ آمَنُوا مِنكُمْ وَعَمِلُوا الصَّالِحَاتِ لَيَسْتَخْلِفَنَّهُمْ فِي الْأَرْضِ الآية، وما أخبر الله من أهوال القيامة وسوق أهل الجنة إليها، وسوق أهل النار، وحصول الزفير والشهيق من الكفار، واستغاثتهم وطلبهم العود إلى الدنيا، وعودهم إلى ما كانوا عليه لوردوا إليها، وإنكار الكفار تبليغ الرسل إليهم وشهادة أمتنا للرسل بذلك وقوله: لَأَمْلَأَنَّ جَهَنَّمَ مِنَ الْجِنَّةِ وَالنَّاسِ أَجْمَعِينَ وغير ذلك مما يتعذر حصره وتعداده، وإنكار هذه الآيات كفر صريح.
وإن قالوا: نعم أخبر الله تعالى بذلك. قيل لهم: أخبر بذلك وهو عالم، أم أخبر وهو بذلك غير عالم؟ فإن قالوا: أخبر بذلك وهو غير عالم ـ قيل: فإذا لا يعرف صحة خبره، ولا يقع للسامعين الثقة بكون ما أخبر على ما أخبر، إذ هذا هو خاصية خبر من أخبر لا عن علم، فلا تقع الثقة بدخول المطيعين الجنة، ودخول الكفرة النار، ولا بحصول الثواب والعقاب، وبتلذذ أهل الجنة في الجنة، وبقائهم خالدين، وتألم أهل النار وبقائهم فيها خالدين. وهذا كفر صريح.
وإن قالوا: أخبر بذلك وهو عالم به قيل: أكان ما أخبر عنه علم به موجودا أم كان معدوما؟ فإن قالوا: كل ذلك كان موجودا. فقد ادعوا وجود البعث بعد الموت ودخول أهل كل دار إياها للحال والناس كلهم للحال في الدار الآخرة مثابون معاقبون. وهذه سوفسطائية محضة.
And it is said to these (opponents): Did God inform about what will happen in the future? If they say: No, then they have denied what God informed the earlier prophets about the tidings of our Prophet Muhammad (peace be upon him), and the glad tidings of Jesus (peace be upon him) about him according to what the Book states, His saying: 'And a bringer of good tidings of a messenger who will come after me whose name is Ahmad.' And what God informed in the Quran about future events such as His saying: 'You will be called to a people of severe might' and His saying: 'You will surely enter the Sacred Mosque, if Allah wills, in safety' and His saying: 'Allah has promised those among you who believe and do righteous deeds that He will surely make them successors upon the earth' — the verse — and what God informed of the terrors of the Resurrection, the driving of the people of Paradise to it, the driving of the people of Hellfire, the occurrence of groaning and gasping from the disbelievers, their cry for help and their request to return to the world, and their return to what they were upon if they were returned to it, and the disbelievers' denial of the messengers' delivery (of the message), and the testimony of our nation to the messengers concerning that, and His saying: 'I will surely fill Hell with jinn and people all together' — and other things whose enumeration is difficult. And denial of these verses is clear disbelief. And if they say: Yes, God informed about that. It is said to them: Did He inform about that while knowing, or did He inform while not knowing it? If they say: He informed while not knowing it — it is said: Then the correctness of His news is not known, and the listeners do not have confidence that what He informed is as He informed, because this is the characteristic of the news of one who informs without knowledge. So there would be no confidence in the entry of the obedient into Paradise, the entry of the disbelievers into Hellfire, nor in the attainment of reward and punishment, nor in the enjoyment of the people of Paradise in Paradise and their eternal abiding, nor in the suffering of the people of Hellfire and their eternal abiding therein. And this is clear disbelief. And if they say: He informed about that while knowing it. It is said: Was what He informed about — that He knew — existent or non-existent? If they say: All of that was existent — then they have claimed the existence of the resurrection after death and the entry of each group into its abode at the present time, and that all people are at present in the Hereafter, rewarded or punished. And this is pure sophistry.
Source pages p. 368

Commentary
This passage is a dialectical refutation of those who deny God's knowledge of future events. The author presents a dilemma. First, he asks: Did God inform about future events in His scriptures? If the opponent denies this, he is refuted by the many explicit predictions in the Quran (e.g., about the coming of Prophet Muhammad, the conquest of Mecca, the succession of believers, the horrors of the Day of Judgment, etc.). Denial of these is clear disbelief. If the opponent admits that God did inform, then the author asks whether God informed while knowing or not knowing. If He informed without knowledge, then His news cannot be trusted, which undermines all divine promises and threats — also clear disbelief. If they say He informed with knowledge, then the author asks whether what He informed about was existent or non-existent at the time of informing. If they claim it was existent, then they absurdly assert that the events of the Hereafter are already happening now, which is pure sophistry (sufistāʾiyya). Thus, the only consistent position is that God knows future events before they occur.

Key Terms
العلم بالمستقبل
الخبر
الكفر

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some think that denying God's foreknowledge is a valid philosophical position.
Correction: The passage shows that it contradicts explicit divine revelations and leads to rejecting core Islamic beliefs.

Checkpoint
What is the consequence of denying that God informed about future events?
A) It is a valid opinion.
B) It amounts to clear disbelief.
C) It only affects minor issues.
D) It is acceptable for non-Muslims.

Key Takeaway
Denying God's foreknowledge means denying the truthfulness of countless Quranic predictions, which is clear disbelief.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
If you have ever doubted that God knows every detail of your future, including your own choices, how does this passage challenge that doubt? Are you willing to surrender that area of uncertainty to His knowledge?
?
The passage declares that denying God's foreknowledge leads to clear disbelief. Is there any area of your life where you live as if God does not know what you will do tomorrow? What step can you take today to align your heart with the reality of His complete knowledge?
?
God's foreknowledge includes both the terrors of Hell and the bliss of Paradise. How does this certainty affect the way you prepare for your own encounter with the Day of Judgment? What specific change will you make in your daily habits because of this truth?

God's Knowledge Guarantees the Reliability of His News
Second branch: God informs without knowledge.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand that if God informed about the future without knowing it, His news could not be trusted, leading to the collapse of all divine promises.

Core Idea
News without knowledge is unreliable, even if from God.

Moving to the second branch, the author assumes the opponent admits that God informed about the future. The key question now is whether God informed while knowing or not. If the opponent says God informed without knowledge, then the very foundation of trust in divine news collapses. The passage explains that a report from one who does not know cannot inspire confidence, and this would undermine all promises of reward and punishment.

Guided Path
1
Read the second conditional
Now assume the opponent admits God informed. Then ask: with or without knowledge?
2
Consider the 'without knowledge' option
If God informed without knowledge, His news cannot be trusted. This undermines all eschatological promises.
Think: if a person who doesn't know tells you something, would you rely on it?
3
Recognize the conclusion
This is also clear disbelief because it destroys the foundation of faith in the unseen.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ويقال لهؤلاء: إن الله تعالى هل أخبر عما يكون في المستقبل؟ فإن قالوا: لا. فقد أنكروا ما أخبر الله تعالى الأنبياء المتقدمين عليهم السلام من أنباء نبينا محمد عليه السلام، وبشارة عيسى عليه السلام به على ما نطق به الكتاب بقوله تعالى: ﴿ وَمُبَشِّرًا بِرَسُولِ يَأْتِي مِنْ بَعْدِى اسْمُهُ أَحَمَدُ ﴾ وما أنبأ الله تعالى في القرآن عن الكائنات من نحو قوله تعالى: ﴿ سَتُدْعَوْنَ إِلَى قَوْمٍ أُولِي بَأْسٍ شَدِيدٍ ﴾ وقوله تعالى: لَتَدْخُلُنَّ الْمَسْجِدَ الْحَرَامَ إِن شَاءَ اللهُ آمِنِينَ ﴿ وقوله تعالى: وَعَدَ اللهُ الَّذِينَ آمَنُوا مِنكُمْ وَعَمِلُوا الصَّالِحَاتِ لَيَسْتَخْلِفَنَّهُمْ فِي الْأَرْضِ الآية، وما أخبر الله من أهوال القيامة وسوق أهل الجنة إليها، وسوق أهل النار، وحصول الزفير والشهيق من الكفار، واستغاثتهم وطلبهم العود إلى الدنيا، وعودهم إلى ما كانوا عليه لوردوا إليها، وإنكار الكفار تبليغ الرسل إليهم وشهادة أمتنا للرسل بذلك وقوله: لَأَمْلَأَنَّ جَهَنَّمَ مِنَ الْجِنَّةِ وَالنَّاسِ أَجْمَعِينَ وغير ذلك مما يتعذر حصره وتعداده، وإنكار هذه الآيات كفر صريح.
وإن قالوا: نعم أخبر الله تعالى بذلك. قيل لهم: أخبر بذلك وهو عالم، أم أخبر وهو بذلك غير عالم؟ فإن قالوا: أخبر بذلك وهو غير عالم ـ قيل: فإذا لا يعرف صحة خبره، ولا يقع للسامعين الثقة بكون ما أخبر على ما أخبر، إذ هذا هو خاصية خبر من أخبر لا عن علم، فلا تقع الثقة بدخول المطيعين الجنة، ودخول الكفرة النار، ولا بحصول الثواب والعقاب، وبتلذذ أهل الجنة في الجنة، وبقائهم خالدين، وتألم أهل النار وبقائهم فيها خالدين. وهذا كفر صريح.
وإن قالوا: أخبر بذلك وهو عالم به قيل: أكان ما أخبر عنه علم به موجودا أم كان معدوما؟ فإن قالوا: كل ذلك كان موجودا. فقد ادعوا وجود البعث بعد الموت ودخول أهل كل دار إياها للحال والناس كلهم للحال في الدار الآخرة مثابون معاقبون. وهذه سوفسطائية محضة.
And it is said to these (opponents): Did God inform about what will happen in the future? If they say: No, then they have denied what God informed the earlier prophets about the tidings of our Prophet Muhammad (peace be upon him), and the glad tidings of Jesus (peace be upon him) about him according to what the Book states, His saying: 'And a bringer of good tidings of a messenger who will come after me whose name is Ahmad.' And what God informed in the Quran about future events such as His saying: 'You will be called to a people of severe might' and His saying: 'You will surely enter the Sacred Mosque, if Allah wills, in safety' and His saying: 'Allah has promised those among you who believe and do righteous deeds that He will surely make them successors upon the earth' — the verse — and what God informed of the terrors of the Resurrection, the driving of the people of Paradise to it, the driving of the people of Hellfire, the occurrence of groaning and gasping from the disbelievers, their cry for help and their request to return to the world, and their return to what they were upon if they were returned to it, and the disbelievers' denial of the messengers' delivery (of the message), and the testimony of our nation to the messengers concerning that, and His saying: 'I will surely fill Hell with jinn and people all together' — and other things whose enumeration is difficult. And denial of these verses is clear disbelief. And if they say: Yes, God informed about that. It is said to them: Did He inform about that while knowing, or did He inform while not knowing it? If they say: He informed while not knowing it — it is said: Then the correctness of His news is not known, and the listeners do not have confidence that what He informed is as He informed, because this is the characteristic of the news of one who informs without knowledge. So there would be no confidence in the entry of the obedient into Paradise, the entry of the disbelievers into Hellfire, nor in the attainment of reward and punishment, nor in the enjoyment of the people of Paradise in Paradise and their eternal abiding, nor in the suffering of the people of Hellfire and their eternal abiding therein. And this is clear disbelief. And if they say: He informed about that while knowing it. It is said: Was what He informed about — that He knew — existent or non-existent? If they say: All of that was existent — then they have claimed the existence of the resurrection after death and the entry of each group into its abode at the present time, and that all people are at present in the Hereafter, rewarded or punished. And this is pure sophistry.
Source pages p. 368

Commentary
This passage is a dialectical refutation of those who deny God's knowledge of future events. The author presents a dilemma. First, he asks: Did God inform about future events in His scriptures? If the opponent denies this, he is refuted by the many explicit predictions in the Quran (e.g., about the coming of Prophet Muhammad, the conquest of Mecca, the succession of believers, the horrors of the Day of Judgment, etc.). Denial of these is clear disbelief. If the opponent admits that God did inform, then the author asks whether God informed while knowing or not knowing. If He informed without knowledge, then His news cannot be trusted, which undermines all divine promises and threats — also clear disbelief. If they say He informed with knowledge, then the author asks whether what He informed about was existent or non-existent at the time of informing. If they claim it was existent, then they absurdly assert that the events of the Hereafter are already happening now, which is pure sophistry (sufistāʾiyya). Thus, the only consistent position is that God knows future events before they occur.

Key Terms
العلم
الخبر
الثقة
الكفر

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some think God can inform about the future without knowing it, similar to human prophets who sometimes speak without knowledge.
Correction: This passage shows that God's attribute of knowledge is necessary for the reliability of His revelation.

Checkpoint
What is the main problem if God informed about the future without knowing it?
A) It would be a miracle.
B) His news would be unreliable.
C) It would prove He is all-powerful.
D) It would only affect minor details.

Key Takeaway
God's knowledge is essential for the trustworthiness of His divine news; without it, all eschatological promises lose their certainty.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
If the Quran's promises about Paradise were uncertain, would you still live as you do today? What does your current reliance on God's news reveal about your heart?
?
When you struggle with doubt about God's promises, do you ever act as if His news is unreliable? How does this lesson call you to repent of that unspoken disbelief?
?
You claim to believe that God knows all things, but do you live with the confidence that His every promise is certain? What specific promise of God are you failing to trust right now, and what step will you take today to change that?

Refuting the Sophistic Claim that God's Knowledge Implies Pre-Existence
Third branch: God's knowledge and the sophistical pre-existence claim.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand that claiming God's knowledge of future events requires their pre-existence is a sophistical fallacy that contradicts common sense.

Core Idea
God knows the future without it being present now.

In the third and final branch, the author assumes that God informed with knowledge. The opponent might then claim that since God knew about the future events, those events must have already been existent at the time of informing. The passage refutes this by showing that this leads to absurd consequences, such as claiming that the Resurrection and Judgment are already happening now, which is pure sophistry.

Guided Path
1
Read the third conditional
Now assume God informed with knowledge. The new question: was the known event existent or non-existent?
2
Understand the 'existent' answer
If they say it was existent, they must claim the Hereafter is already here, which is absurd.
This is labeled 'pure sophistry'.
3
Reflect on the correct position
God knows future events without them being currently existent.
This preserves the temporal order of creation.

Knowledge and Trustworthy Divine Information
Dialectical refutation: God must know to inform truly.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand why God's knowledge is necessary for His information to be trustworthy, and how denying this leads to disbelief.

Core Idea
Divine information without divine knowledge is worthless.

This passage from Imam al-Nasafi presents a powerful dialectical argument. He forces the opponent to confront the logical consequences of denying God's knowledge: if God informed of Paradise and Hell without knowing, then no one can trust those promises. This dismantles the very foundation of faith. Read carefully how the argument unfolds step by step.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage and translation
Begin by reading the Arabic passage once, then the literal translation. Notice the dialogue structure: an objection is raised and answered.
The Arabic uses a conditional structure (إن قالوا... قيل لهم).
2
Identify the dilemma
The author presents two options: God informed with knowledge or without. See how the argument forces the opponent to choose.
3
Trace the consequence
If the opponent chooses 'without knowledge,' the author lists the devastating results: no trust in Paradise, Hell, reward, punishment, eternity. Understand why this follows from the 'characteristic' (خاصية) of one who informs without knowledge.
The list of consequences is deliberately comprehensive.
4
Reflect on the conclusion
The author declares that such a position is clear disbelief. Ask yourself: why is this argument considered decisive in Islamic theology?
This shows that denying an attribute of God (knowledge) leads to rejecting core beliefs.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وإن قالوا: نعم أخبر الله تعالى بذلك. قيل لهم: أخبر بذلك وهو عالم، أم أخبر وهو بذلك غير عالم؟ فإن قالوا: أخبر بذلك وهو غير عالم ـ قيل: فإذا لا يعرف صحة خبره، ولا يقع للسامعين الثقة بكون ما أخبر على ما أخبر، إذ هذا هو خاصية خبر من أخبر لا عن علم، فلا تقع الثقة بدخول المطيعين الجنة، ودخول الكفرة النار، ولا بحصول الثواب والعقاب، وبتلذذ أهل الجنة في الجنة، وبقائهم خالدين، وتألم أهل النار وبقائهم فيها خالدين. وهذا كفر صريح.
If they say: Yes, God Almighty informed of that. It is said to them: Did He inform while knowing, or did He inform while not knowing that? If they say: He informed while not knowing — it is said: Then the correctness of His information is not known, and the listeners do not have confidence that what He informed is as He informed, for this is the characteristic of the news of one who informs without knowledge, so no confidence occurs in the entry of the obedient into Paradise, nor the entry of the disbelievers into Hell, nor in the attainment of reward and punishment, nor in the delight of the people of Paradise in Paradise, their eternal abiding, nor the pain of the people of Hell and their eternal abiding therein. And this is clear disbelief.
Source pages p. 368

Commentary
This passage is an objection-and-answer. The author presents a dialectical argument: after stating that denying Quranic prophecies is clear disbelief, he anticipates an opponent who concedes that God indeed informed of these things. The author then asks a crucial question: did God inform with knowledge or without? If the opponent answers 'without knowledge,' the author demonstrates the disastrous consequence: such information would lack reliability, nullifying all certainty in divine promises and threats—a clear disbelief. The argument forces the opponent to accept God's knowledge or fall into absurdity.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: That God's information could be trustworthy even if He did not know the outcome.
Correction: The passage shows that trust (thiqah) in information depends on the informer's knowledge. Without knowledge, the report lacks the characteristic of reliability, so no confidence can be placed in it.

Checkpoint
What is the consequence if God had informed without knowledge?
A) His knowledge would be incomplete.
B) He would be ignorant.
C) No trust can be placed in any of His promises or threats.
D) It is still valid because He is God.

Key Takeaway
For divine information to be trustworthy, God must have knowledge of what He informs; otherwise, all religious certainty collapses into disbelief.

Have you ever lived carelessly, assuming that the consequences of your sins might not matter because God might not know? How does this passage call you to change your daily awareness of His all-encompassing knowledge?
?
This passage declares that denying God's knowledge is clear disbelief. Is there any part of your heart that hesitates to believe that God knows every detail of your life—including your struggles and failures? What step will you take today to strengthen your conviction that He knows and still invites you to trust His words?

The Dilemma of Existence vs. Non-Existence for Future Events
Imam al-Nasafi exposes the dilemma when opponents admit God's knowledge of future events.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the logical dilemma that arises when opponents admit God's knowledge of future events, and why both horns of the dilemma lead to absurdities.

Core Idea
Future events cannot be labelled existent or non-existent before they happen; both choices lead to absurdity.

Imam al-Nasafi now presents a clever dilemma to opponents who admit God's knowledge of future events. He forces them to answer whether those future events were existent or non-existent at the time of informing. The answer, either way, contradicts their own principles or leads to manifest absurdity.

Guided Path
1
Read the Arabic passage and translation
First, read the original Arabic and the literal translation to get the flow of the argument.
Notice the structure: question, two possible answers, and a concluding remark.
2
Identify the dilemma's two outcomes
The passage presents two possible answers: either the future events were existent or non-existent. Find the consequences the author draws for each.
3
Understand why each outcome fails
If existent, it implies the afterlife is already happening (sophistry). If non-existent, it admits that non-existent things can be known (contradicts opponent's school).
The term 'sufasitaiyya' (sophistry) is key.
4
Consider the author's conclusion
The author says such a flawed doctrine does not need lengthy refutation. Reflect on why this is a powerful rhetorical closing.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وإن قالوا : أخبر بذلك وهو عالم به قيل : أكان ما أخبر عنه علم به موجودا أم كان معدوما؟ فإن قالوا : كل ذلك كان موجودا. فقد ادعوا وجود البعث بعد الموت ودخول أهل كل دار إياها للحال والناس كلهم للحال في الدار الآخرة مثابون معاقبون. وهذه سوفسطائية محضة. وإن قالوا كل ذلك كان معدوما. فقد أقروا بكون المعدوم معلوما، وتركوا مذهبهم. وهذا مذهب يفنى العلم به عن الإطالة في رده وإبطاله. والله الموفق.
If they say: He informed of that while knowing it. It is said: Were those things He informed about, which He knew, existent or non-existent? If they say: All that was existent. Then they have claimed the occurrence of resurrection after death and the entry of the people of each abode into it immediately, and that all people are immediately in the Hereafter rewarded or punished. And this is pure sophistry. If they say: All that was non-existent. Then they have admitted that the non-existent is known, and they have abandoned their school. And this is a doctrine whose knowledge makes superfluous prolongation in refuting and invalidating it. And God is the Grantor of success.
Source pages p. 368

Commentary
This is a second objection-and-answer passage. The opponent now concedes that God informed with knowledge. The author then poses a further dilemma: were the future events (resurrection, paradise, hell) existent or non-existent at the time of informing? If the opponent says they were existent, then they absurdly claim that the afterlife is already happening now—pure sophistry (sufasitaiyya). If they say they were non-existent, then they admit that non-existent things can be known, which contradicts the theological principle (held by some) that the non-existent is unknowable; thus they abandon their own position. The author concludes that such a flawed doctrine does not need lengthy refutation.

Key Terms
موجود
معدوم
سوفسطائية
معلوم

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Future events must be either existent or non-existent literally even from God's timeless perspective.
Correction: From God's knowledge, future events are known as future, not as present existents nor as absolute non-existents; the dilemma exposes the absurdity of forcing a temporal category onto divine knowledge.

Checkpoint
What happens if the opponent says the future events were non-existent?
A) They become sophists.
B) They admit the non-existent is known, contradicting their school.
C) They resort to allegorical interpretation.
D) They deny God's foreknowledge.

Key Takeaway
The dilemma shows that forcing future events into categories of existent or non-existent leads to absurdity, thereby defending the orthodox view of divine knowledge.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you think about future events that haven’t happened yet—like your own death or the Day of Judgment—do you unconsciously imagine them as already 'existing' in God's knowledge? How does this dilemma force you to rethink that assumption? Today, will you consciously affirm that God’s knowledge is beyond such categories, and let that humble your certainty about how He knows?
?
This passage exposes that forcing a complex reality into a simple binary can lead to absurdity. Think of a belief or opinion you hold strongly about Islam or life. Are you perhaps oversimplifying it? Will you take time this week to examine whether you have unintentionally fallen into a false dichotomy, and seek a more nuanced understanding?
?
The opponent's view is dismissed as 'pure sophistry' after their logic collapses. Have you ever been so attached to a theological position that you refused to see its logical flaws? Can you recall a time you clung to an idea even when it led to contradiction? What will you do the next time you feel that resistance—will you surrender to the truth, even if it means abandoning a comfortable belief?

Divine trial manifests pre-eternal knowledge
Refutation of the claim that divine trial implies new knowledge for God.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand that divine trial does not indicate a change in God's knowledge but rather manifests what He already knows eternally.

Core Idea
Divine trial reveals pre-eternal knowledge, not new knowledge.

Imam al-Nasafi refutes the misconception that verses like 'li-na‘lama' imply God acquires knowledge through trial. He explains that such expressions are for manifesting what God already knows.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage carefully
Read the Arabic passage once without analysing. Then read the translation. Notice the refutation of the opponents' claim.
The passage begins with 'And they have no argument...'.
2
Identify the refutation
Find the main claim being refuted: that divine trial is for God to acquire knowledge. Notice how the author contrasts this with the case of creatures.
3
Understand the reinterpretation
The author reinterprets 'li-na‘lama' (that We may know) as 'to know as an existent' or 'to manifest what We knew'. See how he applies this to three verses.
The verses are: 1) 'that We may know who follows the Messenger', 2) 'that We may know which of the two parties', 3) 'that We may see how you work'.
4
Connect to divine omniscience
Reflect on why this interpretation is necessary: to uphold God's omniscience and immutability. The trial is for us, not for God.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ولا تعلق لهم بما تعلقوا به من الآيات، فإن الابتلاء من الله تعالى ليس ليثبت له به العلم كما في حق من يجوز عليه الجهل بالعواقب، بل الابتلاء منه تعالى ليظهر ما علم في الأزل على ما علم به. وكذا قوله تعالى: لِنَعْلَمَ مَن يَتَّبِعُ الرَّسُولَ لنعلم كائنا ما قد علم أنه يكون ولنعلم موجودا ما قد علم أنه يوجد، وكذا قوله: لِنَعْلَمَ أَيُّ الْزَبَيْنِ ليظهر ما كنا علمناه على ما علمناه وقوله تعالى: لِنَنظُرَ كَيْفَ تَعْمَلُونَ أي ليظهر علمكم على ما كان علم والله الموفق.
وكلمة "لعل" من الله واجبة، فكان ذلك إخبارا على القطع لا على الترجي، أو ذكر ذلك لترجية غيره ليفعل ذلك الفعل على رجاء منه أن يحصل المقصود والله أعلم. ولأرباب التأويل في تأويل هذه الآيات كلام طويل فمن أراد الزيادة على ما بينا فعليه الرجوع إلى تصانيفهم، فأما كتابنا هذا فلا يحتمل الاستقصاء في شرح ذلك. وبالله العصمة.
And they have no argument from the verses they cling to, for trial from God Almighty is not to establish knowledge for Him thereby, as in the case of one for whom ignorance of consequences is possible; rather, trial from Him is to manifest what He knew in pre-eternity according to what He knew. Similarly, His statement: 'That We may know who follows the Messenger' [meaning] to know as a being that He already knew would be, and to know as an existent that He already knew would exist. Similarly, His statement: 'That We may know which of the two parties' [meaning] to manifest what We knew according to what We knew. And His statement: 'That We may see how you work' [meaning] to manifest your knowledge according to what He knew. And God is the Grantor of success.
And the word 'la'alla' from God is certain, so that is information with certainty, not with possibility; or it was mentioned to give hope to others to do that action in hope that the intended goal would be attained. And God knows best. And the people of interpretation have lengthy speech in interpreting these verses. Whoever wants more than what we have clarified should refer to their works, for our book does not bear exhaustive explanation of that. And with God is protection.
Source pages p. 369

Commentary
This passage comprises two related clarifications. First, the author refutes the claim that verses such as 'li-na‘lama' (that We may know) imply that God acquires new knowledge through trial. He explains that divine trial (ibtilā') is not for God's benefit (since He is omniscient) but to manifest (izhār) what He already knows eternally. The author provides a semantic interpretation of 'li-na‘lama' as 'li-na‘lama kā’inan' (to know as a being) and similarly for other verses, emphasizing manifestation. Second, he addresses the word 'la‘alla' (perhaps) when used by God. He asserts that it indicates certainty (qat‘), not possibility (tarajjī), or it is used to encourage human action. The author acknowledges that detailed interpretations exist in other works, but his book does not aim to exhaustively cover them. This passage demonstrates the author's method of defending divine transcendence and the certainty of divine speech.

Key Terms
ابتلاء
ليظهر
لنعلم

Key Terms from Source Passage

A) To acquire new knowledge for God.
B) To test humans for new knowledge.
C) To manifest what was already known eternally.
D) To demonstrate God's power.

Key Takeaway
Divine trial does not change God's knowledge; it manifests His eternal knowledge in time.

The word 'la‘alla' from God indicates certainty
Clarification that 'la‘alla' from God is certain, not tentative.

Learning Objective

Core Idea
'Perhaps' from God is certain.

Imam al-Nasafi addresses another objection: that the Qur'anic word 'la‘alla' (perhaps) suggests doubt or possibility in God's speech. He clarifies that from God, it is either a definitive statement of certainty or a means to encourage human effort.

The author gives two possible meanings: either it is a definite statement (qat‘) or it is used to give hope to others to act in hope of attaining a goal.
Both interpretations remove the implication of uncertainty in God.
3

The author acknowledges that there are lengthy discussions in other works, but his book does not aim to be exhaustive. This shows his awareness of broader scholarly discourse.

Deducing Eternal Attributes from God's Descriptions
Imam al-Nasafi infers eternal attributes from God's self-descriptions.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how Maturidi theologians rationally infer the existence of eternal divine attributes from God's essential descriptions.

Core Idea
God's descriptions logically entail real, eternal attributes.

In this passage, Imam al-Nasafi presents a foundational Maturidi argument: because God is described as Living, Powerful, and Knowing in pre-eternity, these descriptions cannot be empty — they necessarily imply corresponding attributes. This reasoning establishes the reality and eternity of divine attributes without abandoning tawhid.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage and translation
Read the Arabic passage once without rushing, then read the literal translation. Notice the logical flow: first establishment of descriptions, then reflection, then conclusion.
The passage ends with 'fa-‘alimnā' indicating a rational certainty.
2
Identify the key inference
Identify the inference: from God being described as Living to the necessity of life as an attribute. Do this for each description (Powerful, Knowing, etc.).
The author uses the phrase 'cannot possibly be without' to show necessity.
3
Reflect on the rational necessity
Ask yourself: Why is it rationally impossible for a living being to be without life? How does this argument support the eternity of attributes?
This is a cornerstone of Maturidi theology distinguishing attributes from essence.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وإذا ثبت أنه تعالى حي قادر سميع بصير عالم، وكان في الأزل ويكون، لا يزال موصوفا بهذه الصفات فبعد ذلك تأملنا فعرقنا أن الحي يستحيل أن يكون بدون الحياة، وكذا القادر والعالم بدون القدرة والعلم، وما وراء ذلك من الصفات، فعلمنا
And when it is established that He, exalted, is Living, Powerful, Hearing, Seeing, Knowing, and He was in pre-eternity and will be, continually described with these attributes, then after that we reflected and knew that the Living cannot possibly be without life, and likewise the Powerful and Knowing cannot be without power and knowledge, and the rest of the attributes beyond that. So we know.
Source pages p. 369

Commentary
This passage presents a rational inference (istidlāl) from God's essential descriptions to the existence of eternal attributes. After establishing that God is described as Living (ḥayy), Powerful (qādir), Hearing (samī‘), Seeing (baṣīr), and Knowing (‘ālim), and that these descriptions are eternal (He was and always will be so), the author reasons that these descriptions necessitate real, eternal attributes: life (ḥayāh), power (qudrah), and knowledge (‘ilm). The argument is that a living being cannot be without life, nor a powerful being without power, etc. The conclusion 'fa-‘alimnā' (so we know) indicates that this knowledge is rationally necessary. This is a foundational Maturidi argument for the reality and eternity of divine attributes.

Key Terms
حي
حياة
قدرة
علم
صفات

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: God's attributes are identical to His essence or merely metaphorical descriptions.
Correction: Al-Nasafi argues that descriptions like 'Living' necessarily entail real attributes (life), distinct from essence yet not separate, because the living cannot be without life.

Checkpoint

C) That life is a metaphorical description.
D) That life is a created attribute.

Key Takeaway
The essential point is that God's eternal descriptions necessitate real eternal attributes, a rational foundation for Maturidi theology.

Eternal Attributes: Neither Essence Nor Other
Nasafi proves divine attributes and defines their relationship to essence.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand why Allah's eternal attributes are real and subsisting in His essence, yet neither identical to His essence nor separate from it.

Core Idea
Allah's attributes are real, distinct yet not separate—neither essence nor other.

The Maturidi position on divine attributes occupies a middle ground between those who deny attributes and those who anthropomorphize. Before we can understand how attributes relate to the essence, we must first establish that they exist. In this passage, Imam al-Nasafi uses a simple logical reflection to prove that Allah has real attributes of life, power, knowledge, hearing, and sight, and then clarifies their precise relationship to the essence and to each other.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage and translation
Read the Arabic passage once without analysing. Then read the literal translation to grasp the overall argument.
Notice the compact style—each word carries weight.
2
Follow the logical deduction
The author reasons: a living being cannot exist without life, so Allah (who is described as living) must have life as a real attribute. Apply the same to power, knowledge, etc.
This is an inference from a known principle to the unseen.
3
Understand the unique formulation
The author states that each attribute is neither the essence nor other than the essence, and similarly each attribute is not identical to nor other than another attribute.
This avoids two extremes: saying attributes are the essence (negating distinction) or that they are separate entities (compromising tawhid).

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وإذا ثبت أنه تعالى حي قادر سميع بصير عالم، وكان في الأزل ويكون، لا يزال موصوفا بهذه الصفات فبعد ذلك تأملنا فعرقنا أن الحي يستحيل أن يكون بدون الحياة، وكذا القادر والعالم بدون القدرة والعلم، وما وراء ذلك من الصفات، فعلمنا أن الله تعالى له حياة وهي صفة له قائمة بذاته، وكذا السمع والبصر والعلم والقدرة، وهذه الصفات لا يقال لكل صفة منها إنها الذات ولا يقال إنها غير الذات، وكذا كل صفة مع ما وراءها كالعلم لا يقال له إنه غير القدرة ولا إنه عينها.
And when it is established that He, exalted, is living, powerful, hearing, seeing, knowing, and that He was in eternity and will be, never ceasing to be described with these attributes, then after reflection we came to know that the living being is impossible without life, and similarly the powerful and knowing being without power and knowledge, and whatever other attributes there may be. Thus we know that Allah, exalted, has life, which is an attribute subsisting in His essence, and similarly hearing, sight, knowledge, and power. And these attributes are not said, each one of them, to be the essence, nor are they said to be other than the essence. Likewise, each attribute in relation to another, such as knowledge, is not said to be other than power nor identical to it.
Source pages p. 370

Commentary
This passage is a proof for the existence of divine attributes. It begins by stating the established fact that Allah is described as living, powerful, hearing, seeing, and knowing eternally. The author then reasons: after reflection, we realize that a living being cannot exist without life; similarly, a powerful being cannot exist without power, and a knowing being cannot exist without knowledge. By analogy, we infer that Allah must have life, power, knowledge, hearing, and sight as real attributes subsisting in His essence. Then a crucial theological principle is stated: these attributes are neither identical to the essence (lā hiya al-dhāt) nor other than the essence (lā hiya ghayr al-dhāt). Moreover, each attribute is not identical to another attribute nor other than it (e.g., knowledge is not said to be other than power nor identical to it). This is the distinctive Maturidi position, avoiding both the Mu'tazila denial of attributes and the anthropomorphic or overly literal identification.

Key Terms
صفات (sifāt)
حياة (hayāh)
قدرة (qudra)
علم ('ilm)
سمع (sam')
بصر (baṣar)
ذات (dhāt)
غير (ghayr)

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Attributes that are not identical to the essence must be other (separate) entities.
Correction: The author states attributes are neither the essence nor other, meaning they are distinct in meaning but not separate existences.

Checkpoint
How does the author describe the relationship between Allah's attributes and His essence?
A) The attributes are identical to the essence
B) The attributes are other than the essence
C) The attributes are neither identical nor other
D) The attributes are created and separate

Key Takeaway
Allah's attributes are real and subsist in His essence, but they are neither identical to His essence nor separate from it, and each attribute is distinct from the others without being entirely other.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?

In what specific action this week will you treat His knowledge—that He sees and hears you—as a reality that changes your behavior?
?
The passage teaches that divine attributes are neither essence nor other. How does this middle path confront your own tendency to either minimize God to abstract essence or to perceive Him as multiple beings? Have you ever caught yourself acting as if one attribute (like mercy) exists without His justice? What must you realign in your daily gratitude and fear?
?
If Allah's attributes are real but not separate from Him, then His hearing of your every whisper is not a secondary thing—it is His very reality. What secret thought or habit have you been hiding from others, thinking it is hidden from Him? Will you expose it to yourself in repentance today, knowing that His knowledge is not separate from His essence?

Divine Attributes

The Maturidi Position on Divine Attributes: Neither Essence Nor Other
Al-Nasafi states the Maturidi view that attributes are neither the essence nor other.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the Maturidi doctrine that divine attributes subsist in the essence without being identical to it or separate from it.

Core Idea
Divine attributes: real but not distinct substances, nor mere labels.

In this passage, Imam al-Nasafi articulates the distinctive Maturidi position on the relation between God's essence and His attributes. He affirms that attributes like life, knowledge, and power are real and subsist in the essence, yet they are neither the essence itself nor completely other than it. This via media avoids the extremes of identity and separation.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage and translation
Read the Arabic passage once, then read the literal English translation. Notice the key phrases 'قائمة بذاته' and 'لا هي الذات ولا غير الذات'.
These phrases are the core of the Maturidi position.
2
Identify the attributes and the rule
List the five attributes mentioned. Then note the two rules: (1) each attribute is neither the essence nor other, (2) each attribute is neither identical to nor other than another attribute.
3
Reflect on the via media
Consider why this middle position is important. How does it differ from saying attributes are identical to the essence (like some Mu'tazila) or entirely separate (like some Ash'aris)?
This helps avoid anthropomorphism and denial of attributes.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
أن الله تعالى له حياة وهي صفة له قائمة بذاته، وكذا السمع والبصر والعلم والقدرة وهذه الصفات لا يقال لكل صفة منها إنها الذات ولا يقال إنها غير الذات، وكذا كل صفة مع ما وراءها كالعلم لا يقال له إنه غير القدرة ولا إنه عينها.
That God Almighty has life, and it is an attribute subsisting in His essence, and likewise hearing, sight, knowledge, and power. And these attributes: it is not said of each attribute that it is the essence, nor is it said that it is other than the essence. Likewise, every attribute with respect to another beyond it, like knowledge: it is not said of it that it is other than power, nor that it is identical to it.
Source pages p. 370

Commentary
This passage defines the Maturidi position on the relation between God's essence and His attributes. Al-Nasafi begins by affirming that God has attributes such as life, hearing, sight, knowledge, and power, and these attributes subsist in His essence (قائمة بذاته). He then clarifies the precise relationship: each attribute is neither identical to the essence (لا يقال إنها الذات) nor completely other than the essence (لا يقال إنها غير الذات). This is a distinctive via media. He extends the same rule to relations between attributes: e.g., knowledge is neither identical to power nor wholly other than it. Thus the attributes are real and distinct from each other and from the essence, yet not separate existences—they are modes of the essence, known only through revelation and reason.

Key Terms
صفة
ذات
قائمة بذاته
لا هي الذات ولا غير الذات

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some confuse the Maturidi position with the Ash'ari view that attributes are distinct from the essence.
Correction: Maturidis explicitly reject both identity and complete otherness, maintaining a nuanced middle position.

Checkpoint
According to the Maturidi position as stated by al-Nasafi, how should we describe the divine attributes in relation to the essence?
A) They are identical to the essence.
B) They are entirely other than the essence.
C) They are neither identical to the essence nor other than it.
D) They are accidental qualities in the essence.

Key Takeaway
The Maturidi view affirms real divine attributes that subsist in the essence, neither identical to it nor separate from it.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
The passage teaches that God's attributes are neither His essence nor other than it. How does this challenge your natural tendency to either reduce God to a single attribute or to think of His attributes as separate parts? Take a moment to identify one such tendency you have, and commit to replacing it with the Maturidi affirmation of mystery.
?
When you call upon God as 'the Merciful' or 'the Powerful,' do you truly believe that mercy and power are real in Him, not just mental labels? The passage insists they are real attributes subsisting in His essence. Does your prayer reflect that belief? Write down one practical change in how you will address God's attributes in your next prayer.
?
If knowledge and power in God are neither identical nor other, how should that affect your trust in His perfect knowledge of your life and His power to help you? Are you willing to accept that His attributes are perfectly united yet distinct, even if your mind cannot fully grasp it? What area of your life needs this trust most right now?

Mu'tazilite Position and First Argument: Otherness Implies Multiplicity
First argument: otherness implies multiplicity

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the Mu'tazilite claim that God has no real attributes and their first argument that any attribute distinct from the essence would be other, leading to multiple eternal entities and violating tawhid.

Core Idea
If attributes are distinct from God, they become rivals to His oneness.

Al-Nasafi begins by stating the Mu'tazilite position: God is living without life, knowing without knowledge. He then presents the first of their four arguments, which focuses on the logical consequence of an attribute being 'other' than the essence. This argument is foundational to their self-identification as 'People of Tawhid'.

Guided Path
1
Read the position and first argument
Read the Arabic passage and its translation. Notice how the Mu'tazilites rephrase divine descriptions (living without life, etc.) and then present the analogy with Zayd and 'Amr.
The analogy draws on everyday otherness to argue about the divine.
2
Identify the core logical move
The argument states: if an attribute is not the essence, it must be 'other' (ghayr). Having multiple eternal others contradicts tawhid. Understand why this would be a problem for Sunni theology.
3
Reflect on the label 'Ahl al-Tawhid'
The Mu'tazilites called themselves 'People of Tawhid' because they saw their view as protecting God's unity. Compare this to the Sunni understanding of tawhid.
This shows how deeply tawhid is at stake.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وزعمت المعتزلة : أن الله تعالى لا حياة له ولا قدرة ولا علم ولا سمع ولا بصر. فهو حي لا حياة له عالم لا علم له، وكذا في الصفات كلها. والذي دعاهم إلى هذا التجاهل شبه منها: أن الصفة إذا لم تكن هي الذات لا محالة فهي غير الذات لا محالة. كزيد لما لم يكن عمرًا كان غير عمرو لا محالة، والقول بإثبات الأشياء المتغايرة في الأزل مناف للتوحيد. ولهذا سموا أنفسهم أهل التوحيد. ومنها أن هذه الصفات لو كان ثابتة لكانت أزلية. إذ القول بحدوث الصفات للقديم محال، وإذا كانت أزلية كانت قديمة، والقدم هو الوصف الخاص لله تعالى فكان القول بثبوت الصفات في الأزل قولا بثبوت الآلهة لإثبات معنى الألوهية وهو القدم للصفات، والقول بالآلهة مناف للتوحيد. ومنها أن الصفات لو ثبتت لكانت باقية، ضرورة، لا وجه إلى القول ببقاء كل صفة منها ببقاء يقوم بها، لاستحالة قيام الصفة بالصفة، فكانت باقية لذاتها، والقول في الغائب بباق للذات مع أن الباقي في الشاهد عند أصحاب الصفات باق بالبقاء يهدم جميع قواعدهم ويؤدي إلى كون الباري تعالى باقيا بلا بقاء، وذا خلاف قولهم. ومنها أن ثبوت هذه المعاني في الشاهد، كان لجواز تعري الذات عن الاتصاف بها لولا ذلك لما عرف ثبوتها، فإن المتحرك لو لم يكن ساكنا في بعض الأزمنة، والأسود أبيض، لما عرف كون الحركة والسواد معنيين وراء الذات. وذا في الغائب مستحيل.
And the Mu'tazilites claimed that God Almighty has no life, no power, no knowledge, no hearing, no sight. So He is living with no life, knowing with no knowledge, and similarly for all attributes. And what led them to this ignorance are doubts, among them: that if the attribute is not the essence, then necessarily it is other than the essence — like Zayd, when he is not 'Amr, he is necessarily other than 'Amr. And the affirmation of diverse things in pre-eternity contradicts tawhid. For this they named themselves 'People of Tawhid'. And among them: that if these attributes were established, they would be eternal. For to say the attributes of the Eternal are originated is impossible. And if they are eternal, they are pre-eternal (qadim), and pre-eternity is the specific description of God Almighty. So affirming attributes in pre-eternity is an affirmation of divinities, because it establishes the meaning of divinity (pre-eternity) for the attributes, and affirming divinities contradicts tawhid. And among them: that if attributes were established, they would necessarily be enduring (baqi). There is no way to say that each attribute endures by an endurance subsisting in it, because it is impossible for an attribute to subsist in an attribute. So they would be enduring by themselves. And to say of the Unseen that something is enduring by itself, while the enduring in the witnessed realm according to the proponents of attributes endures by an endurance, destroys all their principles and leads to the Exalted Creator being enduring without endurance, contrary to their statement. And among them: that the establishment of these meanings (attributes) in the witnessed realm was due to the possibility of the essence being stripped of them; otherwise their establishment would not be known. For if the moving were not sometimes stationary, and the black not white, it would not be known that motion and blackness are meanings beyond the essence. And this is impossible in the Unseen.
Source pages p. 370

Commentary
This passage presents four Mu'tazilite arguments (shubah) against affirming real, eternal attributes for God. Al-Nasafi first states their position: God is living without life, knowing without knowledge, etc. Then he explains their reasoning. The first argument: If an attribute is not identical to the essence, it must be 'other' (ghayr). This otherness in pre-eternity implies multiple eternal entities, violating tawhid. The Mu'tazilites therefore call themselves 'Ahl al-Tawhid'. The second argument: If attributes are eternal, they are pre-eternal (qadim). Since pre-eternity is the distinctive quality of God, affirming eternal attributes means affirming additional gods. The third argument: If attributes are eternal, they must be self-subsisting (baqi bi-dhatihi), because an attribute cannot subsist in another attribute. But in the witnessed world, enduring things endure by an accident of endurance (baqa'). This would force the odd conclusion that God is enduring without endurance, contradicting their own principles. The fourth argument: In the witnessed world, we only know that an attribute is a distinct meaning because the essence can be divested of it (e.g., motion only known because sometimes rest). In the Unseen (God), such divestment is impossible, so we cannot know attributes as distinct. Thus all four arguments aim to show that affirming attributes leads to absurdities contrary to tawhid.

Key Terms
شبه
غير الذات
أزلية
توحيد

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Mu'tazilites deny that God is knowing, powerful, etc.
Correction: They affirm these descriptions but deny they are real, distinct entities; they are the essence itself.

Checkpoint
Why did the Mu'tazilites call themselves 'Ahl al-Tawhid'?
A) Because they affirmed many eternal attributes.
B) Because they believed attributes are identical to the essence.
C) Because they argued that distinct eternal attributes would compromise tawhid.
D) Because they rejected all divine names.

Key Takeaway
The Mu'tazilites argue that if attributes were distinct, they would be 'others' alongside God, violating absolute unity.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you think of God, do you ever feel that describing Him with multiple attributes—like Power, Knowledge, Mercy—somehow divides your heart's focus, making His oneness feel less real? How does this Mu'tazilite concern challenge you to examine the purity of your own tawhid?
?
The Mu'tazilites went to an extreme to protect God's unity, but they ended up denying the reality of His attributes. In your life, are you ever tempted to overcorrect a perceived flaw in your understanding, only to fall into another imbalance? Where do you need to seek the balanced truth of revelation rather than your own logic?
?
This passage shows that even the most sincere seekers of tawhid can build arguments on flawed premises. What is one area of your belief or practice where you might be relying more on human reasoning than divine revelation? How will you commit today to grounding yourself more firmly in the Book and Sunnah, even when it challenges your intellect?

Second Argument: Eternal Attributes Imply Multiple Gods
Second argument: eternal attributes imply multiple gods

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the Mu'tazilite argument that if attributes are eternal, they share the divine quality of pre-eternity (qadim), thus implying multiple gods.

Core Idea
Eternal attributes would be gods themselves.

The second Mu'tazilite argument builds on the first: if attributes are eternal, they must be pre-eternal (qadim). Since pre-eternity is the distinctive attribute of God alone, affirming eternal attributes means affirming multiple pre-eternal entities, i.e., multiple gods.

Guided Path
1
Read the second argument
Read the Arabic and translation for the second shubha. Notice the logical steps: attributes eternal → qadim → qadim is unique to God → multiple qadim = multiple gods.
This is a classic reductio ad absurdum.
2
Analyze the key term 'qadim'
Understand that 'qadim' (pre-eternal) is considered a necessary attribute of God alone. The argument claims that attributing pre-eternity to anything else is shirk.
Sunni theology responds by distinguishing between necessary existence and pre-eternity, but the argument is powerful.
3
Reflect on the implication
Consider why the Mu'tazilites think this argument is decisive against real attributes. How might a Sunni theologian respond?
The argument forces a choice: either attributes are not real, or they are gods.

Third Argument: Attributes Would Be Self-Subsisting
Third argument: attributes would be self-subsisting and cause a contradiction

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the Mu'tazilite argument that eternal attributes must be self-subsisting (baqi bi-dhatihi), which contradicts the Sunni position that things endure by an accident of endurance.

Core Idea
Eternal attributes would be self-enduring, contradicting Sunni ontology.

The third argument focuses on the concept of 'remaining' (baqa'). If attributes are eternal, they must be enduring (baqi). Since an attribute cannot subsist in another attribute (like endurance subsisting in an attribute), attributes would have to endure by themselves. But in the witnessed world, things endure by an accident of endurance (baqa'), leading to a contradiction: God would be enduring without endurance.

Guided Path
1
Read the third argument
Read the Arabic and translation. Understand the terms: 'baqi', 'baqa'' (endurance), and the impossibility of an attribute subsisting in an attribute.
This is a technical argument about ontology of accidents.
2
Identify the self-subsistence claim
The Mu'tazilites say: if attributes endure, they cannot endure by a separate endurance (since attribute cannot inhere in attribute), so they must endure by themselves.
This would make them like substances.
3
See the contradiction
In the witnessed realm (shahid), things that endure do so by an accident. But the Mu'tazilite opponents say God endures by His essence. Here, the argument claims that applying self-subsistence to attributes would lead to God being enduring without endurance, which is contrary to the opponents' own position.
The argument is meant to show inconsistency.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books

Fourth Argument: Unknowability of Attributes in the Unseen
Fourth argument: unknowability of attributes in the Unseen

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the Mu'tazilite argument that we can only know attributes as distinct through their separability from the essence, which is impossible in God (the Unseen).

Core Idea
We cannot know attributes in God because they can never be separated from Him.

The fourth and final argument draws an analogy from the witnessed world: we only know that an attribute is a distinct meaning (like motion) because the essence can exist without it (e.g., rest). Since God's attributes are eternal and inseparable, we cannot know them as distinct realities. Therefore, we should not affirm them as real.

Guided Path
1
Read the fourth argument
Read the Arabic and translation. Notice the examples: motion is known because the moving thing sometimes rests; blackness is known because the thing sometimes is white.
This argument relies on an epistemological principle.
2
Understand the principle of distinction
The argument states that we only know a quality as a distinct meaning (ma'na) when the essence can be stripped of it. In the Unseen (God), His essence cannot be stripped of any attribute, so we cannot know any attribute as distinct.
This is a skeptical argument about our knowledge of God.
3
Apply to God
Since God is eternally knowing, powerful, etc., we never see Him without these. Therefore, we have no basis to say these are real attributes beyond the essence.
The conclusion: we should only affirm them as descriptions, not as distinct entities.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وزعمت المعتزلة : أن الله تعالى لا حياة له ولا قدرة ولا علم ولا سمع ولا بصر. فهو حي لا حياة له عالم لا علم له، وكذا في الصفات كلها. والذي دعاهم إلى هذا التجاهل شبه منها: أن الصفة إذا لم تكن هي الذات لا محالة فهي غير الذات لا محالة. كزيد لما لم يكن عمرًا كان غير عمرو لا محالة، والقول بإثبات الأشياء المتغايرة في الأزل مناف للتوحيد. ولهذا سموا أنفسهم أهل التوحيد. ومنها أن هذه الصفات لو كان ثابتة لكانت أزلية. إذ القول بحدوث الصفات للقديم محال، وإذا كانت أزلية كانت قديمة، والقدم هو الوصف الخاص لله تعالى فكان القول بثبوت الصفات في الأزل قولا بثبوت الآلهة لإثبات معنى الألوهية وهو القدم للصفات، والقول بالآلهة مناف للتوحيد. ومنها أن الصفات لو ثبتت لكانت باقية، ضرورة، لا وجه إلى القول ببقاء كل صفة منها ببقاء يقوم بها، لاستحالة قيام الصفة بالصفة، فكانت باقية لذاتها، والقول في الغائب بباق للذات مع أن الباقي في الشاهد عند أصحاب الصفات باق بالبقاء يهدم جميع قواعدهم ويؤدي إلى كون الباري تعالى باقيا بلا بقاء، وذا خلاف قولهم. ومنها أن ثبوت هذه المعاني في الشاهد، كان لجواز تعري الذات عن الاتصاف بها لولا ذلك لما عرف ثبوتها، فإن المتحرك لو لم يكن ساكنا في بعض الأزمنة، والأسود أبيض، لما عرف كون الحركة والسواد معنيين وراء الذات. وذا في الغائب مستحيل.
And the Mu'tazilites claimed that God Almighty has no life, no power, no knowledge, no hearing, no sight. So He is living with no life, knowing with no knowledge, and similarly for all attributes. And what led them to this ignorance are doubts, among them: that if the attribute is not the essence, then necessarily it is other than the essence — like Zayd, when he is not 'Amr, he is necessarily other than 'Amr. And the affirmation of diverse things in pre-eternity contradicts tawhid. For this they named themselves 'People of Tawhid'. And among them: that if these attributes were established, they would be eternal. For to say the attributes of the Eternal are originated is impossible. And if they are eternal, they are pre-eternal (qadim), and pre-eternity is the specific description of God Almighty. So affirming attributes in pre-eternity is an affirmation of divinities, because it establishes the meaning of divinity (pre-eternity) for the attributes, and affirming divinities contradicts tawhid. And among them: that if attributes were established, they would necessarily be enduring (baqi). There is no way to say that each attribute endures by an endurance subsisting in it, because it is impossible for an attribute to subsist in an attribute. So they would be enduring by themselves. And to say of the Unseen that something is enduring by itself, while the enduring in the witnessed realm according to the proponents of attributes endures by an endurance, destroys all their principles and leads to the Exalted Creator being enduring without endurance, contrary to their statement. And among them: that the establishment of these meanings (attributes) in the witnessed realm was due to the possibility of the essence being stripped of them; otherwise their establishment would not be known. For if the moving were not sometimes stationary, and the black not white, it would not be known that motion and blackness are meanings beyond the essence. And this is impossible in the Unseen.
Source pages p. 370

Commentary
This passage presents four Mu'tazilite arguments (shubah) against affirming real, eternal attributes for God. Al-Nasafi first states their position: God is living without life, knowing without knowledge, etc. Then he explains their reasoning. The first argument: If an attribute is not identical to the essence, it must be 'other' (ghayr). This otherness in pre-eternity implies multiple eternal entities, violating tawhid. The Mu'tazilites therefore call themselves 'Ahl al-Tawhid'. The second argument: If attributes are eternal, they are pre-eternal (qadim). Since pre-eternity is the distinctive quality of God, affirming eternal attributes means affirming additional gods. The third argument: If attributes are eternal, they must be self-subsisting (baqi bi-dhatihi), because an attribute cannot subsist in another attribute. But in the witnessed world, enduring things endure by an accident of endurance (baqa'). This would force the odd conclusion that God is enduring without endurance, contradicting their own principles. The fourth argument: In the witnessed world, we only know that an attribute is a distinct meaning because the essence can be divested of it (e.g., motion only known because sometimes rest). In the Unseen (God), such divestment is impossible, so we cannot know attributes as distinct. Thus all four arguments aim to show that affirming attributes leads to absurdities contrary to tawhid.

Key Terms
شاهد
غائب
معاني
جواز تعري الذات

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
Why does the fourth argument claim we cannot know attributes in God as distinct?
A) Because God's attributes are unknown.
B) Because we cannot observe God's nature directly.
C) Because God's essence can never be without these attributes.
D) Because the witnessed world is different from the Unseen.

Key Takeaway
We can only know an attribute as distinct if its essence can be separated from it; since God's attributes are eternal and inseparable, we cannot know them as real distinct entities.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you think about God's attributes like His knowledge or power, do you unconsciously imagine them as separate 'things' attached to God? How does this argument expose that tendency in your own mind? What will you do to correct it?
?
This argument says we cannot truly know God's attributes as distinct realities. Does that leave you feeling unsettled or perhaps relieved? Why? And how will you respond when you encounter others who claim to have certain knowledge about God's nature?
?
If you had to defend the position that we should affirm God's attributes without claiming to know their distinctness, how would you explain it to someone who is confused? What part of this lesson will stick with you the most the next time you reflect on who God is?

Refutation of Mu'tazilites Using Quranic Evidence
Al-Nasafi refutes Mu'tazilite denial by citing Quranic verses affirming God's attributes.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how Al-Nasafi uses explicit Quranic verses to refute the Mu'tazilite denial of God's attributes of knowledge and power.

Core Idea
The Quran itself affirms God's attributes; rejecting them is to claim superiority over God.

Al-Nasafi now turns to scriptural evidence to counter the Mu'tazilite position. He cites five Quranic verses that explicitly attribute knowledge and power to God. The force of his argument is that if the Mu'tazilites deny these attributes, they are essentially claiming to know God better than God knows Himself — a manifestly absurd position.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage carefully
Read the Arabic passage once without analyzing, then read the translation. Let the rhythm of the verses come through.
The passage uses five distinct Quranic verses.
2
Identify the five verses
List each verse and note which attribute (knowledge or power) it affirms about God.
The phrases 'with His knowledge' and 'power belongs to God' are repeated.
3
Understand the conclusion
Al-Nasafi concludes that Mu'tazilite denial implies they claim to better know God than God Himself. Grasp why this is a strong refutation.
The logic: God says He has knowledge and power; Mu'tazilites say He does not; they thus contradict God's self-description.
4
Reflect on the argument type
Consider why scriptural evidence is decisive in this context: it bases the argument on revelation, which Muslims accept as authoritative.
Al-Nasafi is appealing to common ground—the Quran.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
الرد على شبه المعتزلة: ولنا من الدلائل السمعية قوله تعالى: ﴿ وَلَا يُحِيطُونَ بِشَيْءٍ مِّنْ عِلْمِهِ ﴾ وقوله تعالى: فَاعْلَمُوا أَنَّمَا أُنزِلَ بِعِلْمِ اللهِ، وقوله تعالى: أَنزَلَهُ بِعِلْمِهِ، وقوله تعالى: أَنَّ الْقُوَّةَ لِلَّهِ جَمِيعًا، وقوله تعالى: إِنَّ اللَّهَ هُوَ الرَّزَّاقُ ذُو الْقُوَّةِ الْمَتِينُ. فالله تعالى أثبت لنفسه العلم والقوة. والمعتزلة يأبون ذلك، فإذا هم على زعمهم أعلم بالله تعالى من الله تعالى بنفسه وهذا مما لا يخفى فساده.
The refutation of the Mu'tazilite doubts: And we have from scriptural evidences His statement: 'And they encompass not a thing of His knowledge' (Q. 2:255); and His statement: 'Know that it was sent down with the knowledge of God' (Q. 11:14); and His statement: 'He sent it down with His knowledge' (Q. 4:166); and His statement: 'That power belongs entirely to God' (Q. 2:165); and His statement: 'Indeed, God is the Provider, the Possessor of Power, the Strong' (Q. 51:58). So God Almighty affirmed for Himself knowledge and power. And the Mu'tazilites reject that. Thus they, according to their claim, know God better than God knows Himself, and the corruption of this is not hidden.
Source pages p. 371

Commentary
This passage provides the scriptural refutation of the Mu'tazilite arguments. Al-Nasafi cites five Quranic verses that explicitly affirm God's attributes of knowledge and power. The first verse (2:255, Ayat al-Kursi) states that nothing encompasses His knowledge. The second (11:14) affirms that the Quran was sent down with God's knowledge. The third (4:166) also states 'with His knowledge'. The fourth (2:165) declares that all power belongs to God. The fifth (51:58) describes God as the Provider, Possessor of Power, the Strong. Al-Nasafi concludes that God has affirmed for Himself knowledge and power, yet the Mu'tazilites deny these attributes. This implies they claim to know God better than God knows Himself, which is obviously corrupt. Thus the scriptural evidence directly refutes the Mu'tazilite denial by showing that God attributes these qualities to Himself in the Quran.

Correction: Al-Nasafi uses the Quran's own words to show that God describes Himself with knowledge and power; denying these is to contradict divine speech, not just to ignore a proof-text.

Scriptural Proofs for Divine Knowledge and Power
Imam Nasafi cites five Quranic verses to prove divine knowledge and power and refutes Mu'tazila denial.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how Imam Nasafi uses Quranic verses to affirm divine attributes and refute the Mu'tazila denial.

Core Idea
Allah affirms His own attributes; those who deny them claim to know better than Him.

Imam Nasafi presents a scriptural argument that is both simple and profound: God Himself declares His knowledge and power in the Quran. By citing five clear verses, he establishes that these attributes are firmly rooted in revelation. He then exposes the logical flaw in the Mu'tazila rejection: it implies that they know Allah better than Allah knows Himself.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage carefully
Read the Arabic and English translation of the passage. Focus on each Quranic verse cited and the concluding argument against the Mu'tazila.
Notice the flow from evidence to conclusion to refutation.
2
Identify the five verses
List the five verses and note which attribute (knowledge or power) each supports. The first three emphasize divine knowledge, the last two emphasize divine power.
The verses are quoted from Surah Al-Baqarah, Hud, An-Nisa, and Adh-Dhariyat.
3
Analyze the refutation
Understand the logical consequence Nasafi draws: if the Mu'tazila reject what Allah affirms, they implicitly claim to know Allah better than He knows Himself. This is a reductio ad absurdum.
Consider why this is a powerful refutation in Islamic theology.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ولنا من الدلائل السمعية قوله تعالى: ﴿ وَلَا يُحِيطُونَ بِشَيْءٍ مِّنْ عِلْمِهِ ﴾ وقوله تعالى: ﴿ فَاعْلَمُوا أَنَّمَا أُنزِلَ بِعِلْمِ اللهِ ﴾ وقوله تعالى: ﴿ أَنزَلَهُ بِعِلْمِهِ ﴾ وقوله تعالى: ﴿ أَنَّ الْقُوَّةَ لِلَّهِ جَمِيعًا ﴾ وقوله تعالى: ﴿ إِنَّ اللَّهَ هُوَ الرَّزَّاقُ ذُو الْقُوَّةِ الْمَتِينُ ﴾ فالله تعالى أثبت لنفسه العلم والقوة. والمعتزلة يأبون ذلك، فإذا هم على زعمهم أعلم بالله تعالى من الله تعالى بنفسه وهذا مما لا يخفى فساده
And we have from the scriptural proofs (al-dalā'il al-sam'iyya) His saying, exalted: 'And they do not encompass anything of His knowledge' (2:255) and His saying, exalted: 'Know that it was sent down with the knowledge of Allah' (11:14) and His saying, exalted: 'He sent it down with His knowledge' (4:166) and His saying, exalted: 'That all power belongs to Allah' (2:165) and His saying, exalted: 'Indeed, Allah is the Provider, the Possessor of Strength, the Firm' (51:58). So Allah, exalted, affirmed for Himself knowledge and power. The Mu'tazila reject that, so they claim to be more knowledgeable about Allah, exalted, than Allah, exalted, Himself—and this is something whose corruption is not hidden.
Source pages p. 371

Commentary
This passage presents a scriptural proof for divine attributes. Imam Nasafi first cites five Quranic verses: the first (2:255) mentions that creatures do not encompass His knowledge, implying He has knowledge; the second (11:14) states revelation came by His knowledge; the third (4:166) says He sent it down with His knowledge; the fourth (2:165) declares all power belongs to Allah; the fifth (51:58) describes Him as the Possessor of Strength. The conclusion is that Allah affirmed for Himself both knowledge and power. The Mu'tazila, however, deny these attributes. The Imam then points out the absurd consequence: by denying what God affirms for Himself, the Mu'tazila implicitly claim to know God better than God knows Himself—a clearly corrupt position.

Misconception: Some think these verses only refer to God's actions, not eternal attributes.
Correction: Imam Nasafi uses the verses to affirm that Allah has eternal attributes of knowledge and power, not just actions.

C) The Mu'tazila have no evidence for their view.
D) The Mu'tazila are atheists.

Key Takeaway
Allah's self-revelation in the Quran provides the decisive proof for His attributes, and rejecting that leads to absurdity.
